versions-maven-plugin not updating properties any more  
Date  :-
Mon, 01 Dec 2014 15:59:33 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi all!&#010;&#010;I have two multi-module projects where the first one is a dependency of&#010;the second one. Usually before a release of the second one also the first&#010;one is released and the second one has to update the dependency-version&#010;which is set via a property.&#010;&#010;For this update I use versions-maven-plugin (v2.1) to do the update:&#010;&#010;  mvn -DincludeProperties=mylib.version versions:update-properties&#010;&#010;This used to work, when the released version was for example 1.0-beta-13&#010;and the new development version was 1.0-beta-14-SNAPSHOT.&#010;&#010;After I changed the new development version to always be 1.0-SNAPSHOT the&#010;update via versions-maven-plugin stopped working. I get debugging output&#010;like state from somebody else on StackOverflow:&#010;http://stackoverflow.com/questions/25034556/how-can-i-update-a-property-in-a-maven-pom&#010;&#010;For me this means version 1.0-beta-13/14 are found but than it says&#010;"current winner is: null" and leaves the version unchanged.&#010;&#010;Could this be a bug or am I doing something wrong?&#010;&#010;- martin&#010;&#010;

Re: Uber jar considered harmful?

contents:- 
It all depends how you use them.&#010;&#010;There are some use cases where they make sense.&#010;&#010;Usually these use cases include aggressive shading of the dependencies you&#010;are bundling.&#010;&#010;Some cases where it can be useful:&#010;&#010;* If you are interfacing with a non-maven aware build tool chain - here the&#010;uberjar makes life easier for that toolchain as they only have one&#010;dependency to specify... the gotcha is if you make this the only way for&#010;people to consume then the POM aware build toolchains will end up with&#010;duplicate class hell&#010;&#010;* If you are creating an "App" or CLI utility jar file where people just&#010;run the file directly then it can be easier to give them a single jar&#010;file... but anyone else embedding your "app" will curse you if you only&#010;provide the uberjar&#010;&#010;On 1 December 2014 at 16:59, Benson Margulies &lt;bimargulies@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I don't know about 'harmful', but there are certainly some good ways to&#010;&gt; shoot your toes off.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; My convention is that I only use shaded jars as exports to the non-Maven&#010;&gt; world, I discourage using shaded jars as part of a larger dependency graph.&#010;&gt; I could detail some mishaps which motivated that convention if anyone&#010;&gt; cares.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Mon, Dec 1, 2014 at 11:36 AM, Ron Wheeler &lt;&#010;&gt; rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;&gt; &gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I wrote this in 2011&#010;&gt; &gt; http://blog.artifact-software.com/tech/?p=121&#010;&gt; &gt; which describe our use of aggregation jars.&#010;&gt; &gt; It is, of course, focused on the wonderful advantages that these offer.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; It may have prompted the discussion that you recall so this might give&#010;&gt; you&#010;&gt; &gt; a time-frame to narrow your search.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I may be wrong but I think that Stephen Connolly and Wayne Fay raised&#010;&gt; some&#010;&gt; &gt; issues with the approach. The word "anti-pattern" may have come up.:-)&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Perhaps this will jog some memories.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Ron&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; On 01/12/2014 10:59 AM, Jeffrey E Care wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; I seem to recall a post in the not too distant past where is was at&#010;&gt; least&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; implied (if not outwardly stated) that the use of uber jars was an&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; anti-practice. Name  :- 
&quot;Robert Scholte&quot; &lt;rfscho...@apache.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: AW: Problems with the release plugin  
Date  :-
Mon, 01 Dec 2014 19:00:10 GMT  
contents:- 
Just to be sure that we are on the same page:&#010;Your request is if the maven-release-plugin could be changed, so you can  &#010;specify versions for external (i.e. non reactor/multimodule) dependencies.&#010;I won't allow this unless it can be automated, hence the introduction of  &#010;the VersionPolicy. This is a first step towards a solution as asked by the  &#010;community, which asked for a better way to predict the next version(s).&#010;&#010;Robert&#010;&#010;Op Mon, 01 Dec 2014 00:11:46 +0100 schreef Christofer Dutz  &#010;&lt;christofer.dutz@c-ware.de&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Oh well ... I give up ... so yet another plugin it will be.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I wasn't talking about changing anything at the workflow, just to have  &#010;&gt; one enforced constraint loosended a little if required, but I guess this  &#010;&gt; will never happen.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Chris&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; -----Ursprüngliche Nachricht-----&#010;&gt; Von: Benson Margulies [mailto:bimargulies@gmail.com]&#010;&gt; Gesendet: Sonntag, 30. November 2014 22:22&#010;&gt; An: Maven Users List&#010;&gt; Betreff: Re: Problems with the release plugin&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The release plugin is a tool that does a specified set of steps. It's  &#010;&gt; built out of reusable components. Turning it into MS Word with&#010;&gt; 10,000,000 options is not, in my view, a good plan.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; If you can write down a clear spec for an alternative workflow, you can  &#010;&gt; study the source and make a plugin. That's what the owners of the  &#010;&gt; gitflow-maven-plugin did. It's an alternative release plugin with a  &#010;&gt; different workflow.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Sun, Nov 30, 2014 at 11:44 AM, Christofer Dutz  &#010;&gt; &lt;christofer.dutz@c-ware.de&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt; Unfortunately the world isn't as ideal as I would like it to be. There  &#010;&gt;&gt; are sometimes constraints that lie outside of the reach of the  &#010;&gt;&gt; developer(s) working on the projects build.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; In one case the company I worked for desperately needed to release  &#010;&gt;&gt; parts of a multi module build separately. I know that this comes with  &#010;&gt;&gt; problems, but as long as no other option comes up to reduce the amount  &#010;&gt;&gt; of binary data of a new release having to be transfered over an Edge  &#010;&gt;&gt; mobile connection, they will have to do partial releases.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; In my current case the entire company is being switched from Ant to  &#010;&gt;&gt; Maven. Switching everything in one big step is completely out of the  &#010;&gt;&gt; question. The amount of simultaneous training needed for this is simply  &#010;&gt;&gt; not possible. So we have to go a migration path which brings us closer  &#010;&gt;&gt; and closer to the final goal of having everything in Maven and be able  &#010;&gt;&gt; to use the default maven-release-plugin. But till we are there it feels  &#010;&gt;&gt; like there is no way without patching this plugin in order to have an  &#010;&gt;&gt; easy transition path.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; What about some "legacy" or "quirks" mode for the plugin that allows  &#010;&gt;&gt; such a thing ... it might even output warnings and pages of text  &#010;&gt;&gt; explaining why this mode sucks and should be avoided. All I am asking  &#010;&gt;&gt; for is a way to use the plugin without having to hack it which  &#010;&gt;&gt; acknowledging that I know this is not ideal, but I am willing to accept  &#010;&gt;&gt; the consequences.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Chris&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; -----Ursprüngliche Nachricht-----&#010;&gt;&gt; Von: Benson Margulies [mailto:bimargulies@gmail.com]&#010;&gt;&gt; Gesendet: Sonntag, 30. November 2014 13:52&#010;&gt;&gt; An: Maven Users List&#010;&gt;&gt; Betreff: Re: Problems with the release plugin&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I'm going to attempt a summary here.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The release plugin has a requirement. It must be true that you can go  &#010;&gt;&gt; to the SCM, checkout a brand new copy of the tree rooted at the &lt;scm/&gt;  &#010;&gt;&gt; element, _change the versions_ in the pom(s), and run a build as  &#010;&gt;&gt; configured by the profiles and goals. If that's not true, the release  &#010;&gt;&gt; process will fail, and possibly leave you with a manual cleanup in the  &#010;&gt;&gt; SCM. There are many ways to set up a build that seems just fine but  &#010;&gt;&gt; fails this test.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The top of this thread is a plea for a 'dry run' that is a perfect  &#010;&gt;&gt; simulation of this, so that users can flush this out before it bites  &#010;&gt;&gt; them, and that it should not be hard to ask for this.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; It seems to me that it should not be hard, in a typical automated build  &#010;&gt;&gt; system (Jenkins, etc.) to set up a build that does exactly this.&#010;&gt;&gt; Checkout a clean tree, run the maven-versions-plugin to set a dummy  &#010;&gt;&gt; version, and run a build, with profiles and goals to match the eventual  &#010;&gt;&gt; release. Eat one of these apples every day, and you won't be visiting  &#010;&gt;&gt; the maven doctor so often.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; It seems to me that it should also not be terribly hard to make this a  &#010;&gt;&gt; feature of the maven-release-plugin.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; As a further wrinkle, there's the question of tag management, which  &#010;&gt;&gt; might be seen as interrelated to the lengthy threads here and elsewhere  &#010;&gt;&gt; about never, ever, deleting a tag. I wonder about yet another m-r-p  &#010;&gt;&gt; parameter: a staging SCM URL, distinct from the &lt;scm/&gt; stock  &#010;&gt;&gt; identifiers. m-r-p would pull from &lt;scm/&gt; but push to this other place.  &#010;&gt;&gt; Then, a human could decide if the release is real, and, if so, push the  &#010;&gt;&gt; commits and tag to the real, immutable, repo. I'm not qualifier to  &#010;&gt;&gt; judge whether this can work for anything other than git, but git sure  &#010;&gt;&gt; is popular.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Dezember 2014 20:00&#010;An: Maven Users List&#010;Betreff: Re: AW: Problems with the release plugin&#010;&#010;Just to be sure that we are on the same page:&#010;Your request is if the maven-release-plugin could be changed, so you can specify versions&#010;for external (i.e. non reactor/multimodule) dependencies.&#010;I won't allow this unless it can be automated, hence the introduction of the VersionPolicy.&#010;This is a first step towards a solution as asked by the community, which asked for a better&#010;way to predict the next version(s).&#010;&#010;Robert&#010;&#010;Op Mon, 01 Dec 2014 00:11:46 +0100 schreef Christofer Dutz&#010;&lt;christofer.dutz@c-ware.de&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Oh well ... November 2014 22:22&#010;&gt; An: Maven Users List&#010;&gt; Betreff: Re: Problems with the release plugin&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The release plugin is a tool that does a specified set of steps. It's &#010;&gt; built out of reusable components. Turning it into MS Word with&#010;&gt; 10,000,000 options is not, in my view, a good plan.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; If you can write down a clear spec for an alternative workflow, you &#010;&gt; can study the source and make a plugin. That's what the owners of the &#010;&gt; gitflow-maven-plugin did. It's an alternative release plugin with a &#010;&gt; different workflow.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Sun, Nov 30, 2014 at 11:44 AM, Christofer Dutz &#010;&gt; &lt;christofer.dutz@c-ware.de&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt; Unfortunately the world isn't as ideal as I would like it to be. &#010;&gt;&gt; There are sometimes constraints that lie outside of the reach of the&#010;&gt;&gt; developer(s) working on the projects build.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; In one case the company I worked for desperately needed to release &#010;&gt;&gt; parts of a multi module build separately. I know that this comes with &#010;&gt;&gt; problems, but as long as no other option comes up to reduce the &#010;&gt;&gt; amount of binary data of a new release having to be transfered over &#010;&gt;&gt; an Edge mobile connection, they will have to do partial releases.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; In my current case the entire company is being switched from Ant to &#010;&gt;&gt; Maven. Switching everything in one big step is completely out of the &#010;&gt;&gt; question. The amount of simultaneous training needed for this is &#010;&gt;&gt; simply not possible. So we have to go a migration path which brings &#010;&gt;&gt; us closer and closer to the final goal of having everything in Maven &#010;&gt;&gt; and be able to use the default maven-release-plugin. But till we are &#010;&gt;&gt; there it feels like there is no way without patching this plugin in &#010;&gt;&gt; order to have an easy transition path.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; What about some "legacy" or "quirks" mode for the plugin that allows &#010;&gt;&gt; such a thing ... it might even output warnings and pages of text &#010;&gt;&gt; explaining why this mode sucks and should be avoided. All I am asking &#010;&gt;&gt; for is a way to use the plugin without having to hack it which &#010;&gt;&gt; acknowledging that I know this is not ideal, but I am willing to &#010;&gt;&gt; accept the consequences.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Chris&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; -----Ursprüngliche Nachricht-----&#010;&gt;&gt; Von: Benson Margulies [mailto:bimargulies@gmail.com]&#010;&gt;&gt; Gesendet: Sonntag, 30. November 2014 13:52&#010;&gt;&gt; An: Maven Users List&#010;&gt;&gt; Betreff: Re: Problems with the release plugin&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I'm going to attempt a summary here.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The release plugin has a requirement. It must be true that you can go &#010;&gt;&gt; to the SCM, checkout a brand new copy of the tree rooted at the &#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;scm/&gt; element, _change the versions_ in the pom(s), and run a build &#010;&gt;&gt; as configured by the profiles and goals. If that's not true, the &#010;&gt;&gt; release process will fail, and possibly leave you with a manual &#010;&gt;&gt; cleanup in the SCM. There are many ways to set up a build that seems &#010;&gt;&gt; just fine but fails this test.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The top of this thread is a plea for a 'dry run' that is a perfect &#010;&gt;&gt; simulation of this, so that users can flush this out before it bites &#010;&gt;&gt; them, and that it should not be hard to ask for this.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; It seems to me that it should not be hard, in a typical automated &#010;&gt;&gt; build system (Jenkins, etc.) to set up a build that does exactly this.&#010;&gt;&gt; Checkout a clean tree, run the maven-versions-plugin to set a dummy &#010;&gt;&gt; version, and run a build, with profiles and goals to match the &#010;&gt;&gt; eventual release. Eat one of these apples every day, and you won't be &#010;&gt;&gt; visiting the maven doctor so often.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; It seems to me that it should also not be terribly hard to make this &#010;&gt;&gt; a feature of the maven-release-plugin.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; As a further wrinkle, there's the question of tag management, which &#010;&gt;&gt; might be seen as interrelated to the lengthy threads here and &#010;&gt;&gt; elsewhere about never, ever, deleting a tag. I wonder about yet &#010;&gt;&gt; another m-r-p&#010;&gt;&gt; parameter: a staging SCM URL, distinct from the &lt;scm/&gt; stock &#010;&gt;&gt; identifiers. m-r-p would pull from &lt;scm/&gt; but push to this other place.&#010;&gt;&gt; Then, a human could decide if the release is real, and, if so, push &#010;&gt;&gt; the commits and tag to the real, immutable, repo. for&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; version 3). Apache Maven puts a lot of emphasis on versions of&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; dependencies&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; and plugins... you could say that versions are very important to&#010;&gt; Maven.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; The colours of the feather were changed to solid colours to match the&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; owl&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; mascot's scarf, beak and eyebrows&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; Voting rules&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; =========&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; Anyone who is subscribed to the dev or users list is eligible to&#010;&gt; vote.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; If you vote multiple times, only your final vote will be counted.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; The vote will be open until 1:00pm GMT on Wed 3rd Dec 2014&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; The vote is for all three changes as one single change. Partial votes&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; (e.g.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; for the logo but not the mascot, or vice-versa) will not be counted.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; I, as the caller of the vote, reserve the right to cancel the vote if&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; this&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; vote is putting the harmony of the community at risk.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; If a majority of the PMC believe that this vote is putting the&#010;&gt; harmony&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; of&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; the community at risk, then the PMC may cancel this vote (though if&#010;&gt; even&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; a&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; small minority of the PMC were of that belief, I will more than&#010;&gt; likely&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; have&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; cancelled the vote before the PMC would need to decide... Name  :- 
Eric Kolotyluk &lt;eric.koloty...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Emotional Support Group for Typesafe Maven Users  
Date  :-
Wed, 03 Dec 2014 19:11:25 GMT  
contents:- 
Does anyone know of a good emotional support group for people trying to &#010;use Maven with Typesafe projects such as Akka and Play?&#010;&#010;I was thinking maybe there could a buddy/sponsor system, such as used in &#010;AA and other self help groups. Maybe there might be group sessions where &#010;people can talk about their trauma, especially by being constantly &#010;invalidated by comments such as "you should use the simple build tool &#010;SBT, cause, well you know, it's simple and easy to use."&#010;&#010;Seriously though, is there a community of people who are successfully &#010;using Maven with Akka an Play projects? I would love to meet you.&#010;&#010;I can see why people who have tried Maven naturally think "oh, its' too &#010;complicated, anyone can write a simple build tool that does what Maven &#010;does." Clearly they do not appreciate what Maven is or what it does. SBT &#010;and Gradle are two great examples of projects that attempted to do &#010;something more simple, but in the end, really don't measure up.&#010;&#010;I personally think the Scala community would be been better served if &#010;more investment was made in developing better Scala build tools within &#010;the Maven framework. More and better plugins for Scala, Akka, Play, &#010;etc.  Better use of&#010;&#010;http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/sect-scala-script-inline.html&#010;http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/ch03s03.html&#010;&#010;I don't know if there is a Scala template for writing Maven plugins (or &#010;mojos), but there should be.&#010;&#010;The more I use SBT, the less I like it. It is not what I consider a &#010;serious build tool for build engineers, it is a toy or playground for &#010;Scala hackers who thrive on the abstruse. Don't get me wrong, I love &#010;Scala, but creating a build tool around .scala files just invites the &#010;use of chicken tracks and obscure overly concise cleverness that leads &#010;to one WTF experience after another. /It is actually possible to write &#010;Scala code that you can reason about,/ but it just as easy to write &#010;Scala code that resembles APL, and reasoning about build engineering was &#010;clearly not a priority with the designers of SBT.&#010;&#010;The Scala-IDE was a really great approach because it leveraged off of an &#010;existing IDE infrastructure such as Eclipse, rather than trying to write &#010;an IDE from scratch the way SBT does. I wish the Scala/Typesafe &#010;community had taken the same approach with build-tools.&#010;&#010;- Eric&#010;&#010;

I can offer you this:&#010;&#010;  http://play.textadventures.co.uk/Play.aspx?id=zv-wer8keey6rnhk4am25q&#010;&#010;It's a create-your-own-adventure about my experience of trying to publish a&#010;library to Maven Central. It's a couple of years old now, so the landscape&#010;might have improved a little in patches.&#010;&#010;Jon&#010;&#010;On 3 December 2014 at 19:11, Eric Kolotyluk &lt;eric.kolotyluk@gmail.com&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt;  Does anyone know of a good emotional support group for people trying to&#010;&gt; use Maven with Typesafe projects such as Akka and Play?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I was thinking maybe there could a buddy/sponsor system, such as used in&#010;&gt; AA and other self help groups. Maybe there might be group sessions where&#010;&gt; people can talk about their trauma, especially by being constantly&#010;&gt; invalidated by comments such as "you should use the simple build tool SBT,&#010;&gt; cause, well you know, it's simple and easy to use."&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Seriously though, is there a community of people who are successfully&#010;&gt; using Maven with Akka an Play projects? I would love to meet you.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I can see why people who have tried Maven naturally think "oh, its' too&#010;&gt; complicated, anyone can write a simple build tool that does what Maven&#010;&gt; does." Clearly they do not appreciate what Maven is or what it does. SBT&#010;&gt; and Gradle are two great examples of projects that attempted to do&#010;&gt; something more simple, but in the end, really don't measure up.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I personally think the Scala community would be been better served if more&#010;&gt; investment was made in developing better Scala build tools within the Maven&#010;&gt; framework. More and better plugins for Scala, Akka, Play, etc.  Better use&#010;&gt; of&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/sect-scala-script-inline.html&#010;&gt; http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/ch03s03.html&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I don't know if there is a Scala template for writing Maven plugins (or&#010;&gt; mojos), but there should be.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The more I use SBT, the less I like it. It is not what I consider a&#010;&gt; serious build tool for build engineers, it is a toy or playground for Scala&#010;&gt; hackers who thrive on the abstruse. Don't get me wrong, I love Scala, but&#010;&gt; creating a build tool around .scala files just invites the use of chicken&#010;&gt; tracks and obscure overly concise cleverness that leads to one WTF&#010;&gt; experience after another. *It is actually possible to write Scala code&#010;&gt; that you can reason about,* but it just as easy to write Scala code that&#010;&gt; resembles APL, and reasoning about build engineering was clearly not a&#010;&gt; priority with the designers of SBT.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The Scala-IDE was a really great approach because it leveraged off of an&#010;&gt; existing IDE infrastructure such as Eclipse, rather than trying to write an&#010;&gt; IDE from scratch the way SBT does. I wish the Scala/Typesafe community had&#010;&gt; taken the same approach with build-tools.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; - Eric&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; You received this message because you are subscribed to the Google Groups&#010;&gt; "scala-debate" group.&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe from this group and stop receiving emails from it, send an&#010;&gt; email to scala-debate+unsubscribe@googlegroups.com.&#010;&gt; For more options, visit https://groups.google.com/d/optout.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Jon Pretty | @propensive&#010;&#010;

Very good :-)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have published to Maven Central, so I know how daunting this can be at&#010;&gt; first.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; If you want to publish to Maven Central I recommend&#010;&gt; https://www.packtpub.com/application-development/&#010;&gt; getting-started-apache-maven-video&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Cheers, Eric&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 12/3/2014 11:27 AM, Jon Pretty wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I can offer you this:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; http://play.textadventures.co.uk/Play.aspx?id=zv-wer8keey6rnhk4am25q&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; It's a create-your-own-adventure about my experience of trying to publish&#010;&gt;&gt; a library to Maven Central. Maybe there might be group&#010;&gt;&gt;     sessions where people can talk about their trauma, especially by&#010;&gt;&gt;     being constantly invalidated by comments such as "you should use&#010;&gt;&gt;     the simple build tool SBT, cause, well you know, it's simple and&#010;&gt;&gt;     easy to use."&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     Seriously though, is there a community of people who are&#010;&gt;&gt;     successfully using Maven with Akka an Play projects? I would love&#010;&gt;&gt;     to meet you.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     I can see why people who have tried Maven naturally think "oh,&#010;&gt;&gt;     its' too complicated, anyone can write a simple build tool that&#010;&gt;&gt;     does what Maven does." Clearly they do not appreciate what Maven&#010;&gt;&gt;     is or what it does. SBT and Gradle are two great examples of&#010;&gt;&gt;     projects that attempted to do something more simple, but in the&#010;&gt;&gt;     end, really don't measure up.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     I personally think the Scala community would be been better served&#010;&gt;&gt;     if more investment was made in developing better Scala build tools&#010;&gt;&gt;     within the Maven framework. More and better plugins for Scala,&#010;&gt;&gt;     Akka, Play, etc.  Better use of&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/sect-&#010;&gt;&gt; scala-script-inline.html&#010;&gt;&gt;     http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/ch03s03.html&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     I don't know if there is a Scala template for writing Maven&#010;&gt;&gt;     plugins (or mojos), but there should be.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     The more I use SBT, the less I like it. It is not what I consider&#010;&gt;&gt;     a serious build tool for build engineers, it is a toy or&#010;&gt;&gt;     playground for Scala hackers who thrive on the abstruse. Don't get&#010;&gt;&gt;     me wrong, I love Scala, but creating a build tool around .scala&#010;&gt;&gt;     files just invites the use of chicken tracks and obscure overly&#010;&gt;&gt;     concise cleverness that leads to one WTF experience after another.&#010;&gt;&gt;     /It is actually possible to write Scala code that you can reason&#010;&gt;&gt;     about,/ but it just as easy to write Scala code that resembles&#010;&gt;&gt;     APL, and reasoning about build engineering was clearly not a&#010;&gt;&gt;     priority with the designers of SBT.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     The Scala-IDE was a really great approach because it leveraged off&#010;&gt;&gt;     of an existing IDE infrastructure such as Eclipse, rather than&#010;&gt;&gt;     trying to write an IDE from scratch the way SBT does. I wish the&#010;&gt;&gt;     Scala/Typesafe community had taken the same approach with build-tools.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     - Eric&#010;&gt;&gt;     --     You received this message because you are subscribed to the&#010;&gt;&gt; Google&#010;&gt;&gt;     Groups "scala-debate" group.&#010;&gt;&gt;     To unsubscribe from this group and stop receiving emails from it,&#010;&gt;&gt;     send an email to scala-debate+unsubscribe@googlegroups.com&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;mailto:scala-debate+unsubscribe@googlegroups.com&gt;.&#010;&gt;&gt;     For more options, visit https://groups.google.com/d/optout.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; --&#010;&gt;&gt; Jon Pretty | @propensive&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Play *very* firmly wants you to use the activator framework to control your&#010;build and deploy - I'd seriously not try and fight against it.  It's one of&#010;the reasons we dropped the Play framework for a community project we're&#010;working on, that and the constant breaking of APIs etc :-).&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;Martijn&#010;&#010;On 4 December 2014 at 12:58, Jeff Jensen &lt;jeffjensen@upstairstechnology.com&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; &gt; If you want to publish to Maven Central I recommend&#010;&gt; https://www.packtpub.com/application-development/&#010;&gt; getting-started-apache-maven-video&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; In case it helps, I've helped a few deploy to Central and recommend this&#010;&gt; (and the other pages on the "Producers" menu); makes it very easy:&#010;&gt; http://central.sonatype.org/pages/ossrh-guide.html&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Wed, Dec 3, 2014 at 3:53 PM, Eric Kolotyluk &lt;eric.kolotyluk@gmail.com&gt;&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Ha ha ha. It's a couple of years old now, so the&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; landscape might have improved a little in patches.&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; Jon&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; On 3 December 2014 at 19:11, Eric Kolotyluk &lt;eric.kolotyluk@gmail.com&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; &lt;mailto:eric.kolotyluk@gmail.com&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     Does anyone know of a good emotional support group for people&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     trying to use Maven with Typesafe projects such as Akka and Play?&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     I was thinking maybe there could a buddy/sponsor system, such as&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     used in AA and other self help groups. Maybe there might be group&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     sessions where people can talk about their trauma, especially by&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     being constantly invalidated by comments such as "you should use&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     the simple build tool SBT, cause, well you know, it's simple and&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     easy to use."&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     Seriously though, is there a community of people who are&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     successfully using Maven with Akka an Play projects? I would love&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     to meet you.&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     I can see why people who have tried Maven naturally think "oh,&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     its' too complicated, anyone can write a simple build tool that&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     does what Maven does." Clearly they do not appreciate what Maven&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     is or what it does. SBT and Gradle are two great examples of&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     projects that attempted to do something more simple, but in the&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     end, really don't measure up.&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     I personally think the Scala community would be been better served&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     if more investment was made in developing better Scala build tools&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;     within the Maven framework. More and better plugins for Scala,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      Akka, Play, etc.  Better use of&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/sect-&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; scala-script-inline.html&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/ch03s03.html&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      I don't know if there is a Scala template for writing Maven&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      plugins (or mojos), but there should be.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      The more I use SBT, the less I like it. It is not what I consider&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      a serious build tool for build engineers, it is a toy or&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      playground for Scala hackers who thrive on the abstruse. Don't get&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      me wrong, I love Scala, but creating a build tool around .scala&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      files just invites the use of chicken tracks and obscure overly&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      concise cleverness that leads to one WTF experience after another.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      /It is actually possible to write Scala code that you can reason&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      about,/ but it just as easy to write Scala code that resembles&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      APL, and reasoning about build engineering was clearly not a&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      priority with the designers of SBT.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      The Scala-IDE was a really great approach because it leveraged off&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      of an existing IDE infrastructure such as Eclipse, rather than&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      trying to write an IDE from scratch the way SBT does. I wish the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      Scala/Typesafe community had taken the same approach with&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; build-tools.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      - Eric&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      --     You received this message because you are subscribed to the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Google&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      Groups "scala-debate" group.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      To unsubscribe from this group and stop receiving emails from it,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      send an email to scala-debate+unsubscribe@googlegroups.com&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      &lt;mailto:scala-debate+unsubscribe@googlegroups.com&gt;.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;      For more options, visit https://groups.google.com/d/optout.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; --&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Jon Pretty | @propensive&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Maybe there might be group sessions where&#010;&gt;&gt; people can talk about their trauma, especially by being constantly&#010;&gt;&gt; invalidated by comments such as "you should use the simple build tool SBT,&#010;&gt;&gt; cause, well you know, it's simple and easy to use."&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Seriously though, is there a community of people who are successfully&#010;&gt;&gt; using Maven with Akka an Play projects? I would love to meet you.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I can see why people who have tried Maven naturally think "oh, its' too&#010;&gt;&gt; complicated, anyone can write a simple build tool that does what Maven&#010;&gt;&gt; does." Clearly they do not appreciate what Maven is or what it does. SBT&#010;&gt;&gt; and Gradle are two great examples of projects that attempted to do&#010;&gt;&gt; something more simple, but in the end, really don't measure up.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I personally think the Scala community would be been better served if more&#010;&gt;&gt; investment was made in developing better Scala build tools within the Maven&#010;&gt;&gt; framework. More and better plugins for Scala, Akka, Play, etc.  Better use&#010;&gt;&gt; of&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/sect-scala-script-inline.html&#010;&gt;&gt; http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/ch03s03.html&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I don't know if there is a Scala template for writing Maven plugins (or&#010;&gt;&gt; mojos), but there should be.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The more I use SBT, the less I like it. It is not what I consider a&#010;&gt;&gt; serious build tool for build engineers, it is a toy or playground for Scala&#010;&gt;&gt; hackers who thrive on the abstruse. Don't get me wrong, I love Scala, but&#010;&gt;&gt; creating a build tool around .scala files just invites the use of chicken&#010;&gt;&gt; tracks and obscure overly concise cleverness that leads to one WTF&#010;&gt;&gt; experience after another. *It is actually possible to write Scala code&#010;&gt;&gt; that you can reason about,* but it just as easy to write Scala code that&#010;&gt;&gt; resembles APL, and reasoning about build engineering was clearly not a&#010;&gt;&gt; priority with the designers of SBT.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The Scala-IDE was a really great approach because it leveraged off of an&#010;&gt;&gt; existing IDE infrastructure such as Eclipse, rather than trying to write an&#010;&gt;&gt; IDE from scratch the way SBT does. I wish the Scala/Typesafe community had&#010;&gt;&gt; taken the same approach with build-tools.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; - Eric&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; --&#010;&gt;&gt; You received this message because you are subscribed to the Google Groups&#010;&gt;&gt; "scala-debate" group.&#010;&gt;&gt; To unsubscribe from this group and stop receiving emails from it, send an&#010;&gt;&gt; email to scala-debate+unsubscribe@googlegroups.com.&#010;&gt;&gt; For more options, visit https://groups.google.com/d/optout.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; -- &#010;&gt; Jon Pretty | @propensive&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

I just want to say that maven is not at all flowers, their phase model is&#010;too primitive, to the point where something such as wsimport (pretty basic&#010;stuff for good ol' java) did not work properly: I had a configuration for&#010;the java version wanted in the pom.xml, but because of the way phases work&#010;and the very restricted compile order, wsimport would always pick my&#010;OS-globally configured wsimport instead of the one configured in the&#010;pom.xml, leading to incorrect defintions of the ws and a VERY ugly hack&#010;where I had to basically compile the thing twice to get it right. Also, my&#010;os installed java was java7, the pom.xml stated that I wanted java6, guess&#010;what version would the .class generated by wsimport be..&#010;&#010;My point is, build tools are no easy task, and I know no system that does&#010;it right. While my experience with sbt has certainly not been yours (and&#010;I've done quite a bit with it, same with maven, where I had written several&#010;plugins for our own dev environment), I do have to say that I find it an&#010;improvement over maven.&#010;&#010;I still love maven for what it accomplished though.&#010;&#010;Cheers.&#010;&#010;On Wed, Dec 3, 2014 at 5:11 PM, Eric Kolotyluk &lt;eric.kolotyluk@gmail.com&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt;  Does anyone know of a good emotional support group for people trying to&#010;&gt; use Maven with Typesafe projects such as Akka and Play?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I was thinking maybe there could a buddy/sponsor system, such as used in&#010;&gt; AA and other self help groups. Maybe there might be group sessions where&#010;&gt; people can talk about their trauma, especially by being constantly&#010;&gt; invalidated by comments such as "you should use the simple build tool SBT,&#010;&gt; cause, well you know, it's simple and easy to use."&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Seriously though, is there a community of people who are successfully&#010;&gt; using Maven with Akka an Play projects? I would love to meet you.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I can see why people who have tried Maven naturally think "oh, its' too&#010;&gt; complicated, anyone can write a simple build tool that does what Maven&#010;&gt; does." Clearly they do not appreciate what Maven is or what it does. SBT&#010;&gt; and Gradle are two great examples of projects that attempted to do&#010;&gt; something more simple, but in the end, really don't measure up.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I personally think the Scala community would be been better served if more&#010;&gt; investment was made in developing better Scala build tools within the Maven&#010;&gt; framework. More and better plugins for Scala, Akka, Play, etc.  Better use&#010;&gt; of&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/sect-scala-script-inline.html&#010;&gt; http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/ch03s03.html&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I don't know if there is a Scala template for writing Maven plugins (or&#010;&gt; mojos), but there should be.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The more I use SBT, the less I like it. It is not what I consider a&#010;&gt; serious build tool for build engineers, it is a toy or playground for Scala&#010;&gt; hackers who thrive on the abstruse. Don't get me wrong, I love Scala, but&#010;&gt; creating a build tool around .scala files just invites the use of chicken&#010;&gt; tracks and obscure overly concise cleverness that leads to one WTF&#010;&gt; experience after another. *It is actually possible to write Scala code&#010;&gt; that you can reason about,* but it just as easy to write Scala code that&#010;&gt; resembles APL, and reasoning about build engineering was clearly not a&#010;&gt; priority with the designers of SBT.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The Scala-IDE was a really great approach because it leveraged off of an&#010;&gt; existing IDE infrastructure such as Eclipse, rather than trying to write an&#010;&gt; IDE from scratch the way SBT does. I wish the Scala/Typesafe community had&#010;&gt; taken the same approach with build-tools.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; - Eric&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; You received this message because you are subscribed to the Google Groups&#010;&gt; "scala-debate" group.&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe from this group and stop receiving emails from it, send an&#010;&gt; email to scala-debate+unsubscribe@googlegroups.com.&#010;&gt; For more options, visit https://groups.google.com/d/optout.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Maybe there might be group sessions where&#010;&gt; &gt; people can talk about their trauma, especially by being constantly&#010;&gt; &gt; invalidated by comments such as "you should use the simple build tool SBT,&#010;&gt; &gt; cause, well you know, it's simple and easy to use."&#010;&gt; &gt; &#010;&gt; &gt; Seriously though, is there a community of people who are successfully&#010;&gt; &gt; using Maven with Akka an Play projects? I would love to meet you.&#010;&gt; &gt; &#010;&gt; &gt; I can see why people who have tried Maven naturally think "oh, its' too&#010;&gt; &gt; complicated, anyone can write a simple build tool that does what Maven&#010;&gt; &gt; does." Clearly they do not appreciate what Maven is or what it does. SBT&#010;&gt; &gt; and Gradle are two great examples of projects that attempted to do&#010;&gt; &gt; something more simple, but in the end, really don't measure up.&#010;&gt; &gt; &#010;&gt; &gt; I personally think the Scala community would be been better served if more&#010;&gt; &gt; investment was made in developing better Scala build tools within the&#010;&gt; &gt; Maven&#010;&gt; &gt; framework. More and better plugins for Scala, Akka, Play, etc.  Better use&#010;&gt; &gt; of&#010;&gt; &gt; &#010;&gt; &gt; http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/sect-scala-script-inline.htm&#010;&gt; &gt; l&#010;&gt; &gt; http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/ch03s03.html&#010;&gt; &gt; &#010;&gt; &gt; I don't know if there is a Scala template for writing Maven plugins (or&#010;&gt; &gt; mojos), but there should be.&#010;&gt; &gt; &#010;&gt; &gt; The more I use SBT, the less I like it. It is not what I consider a&#010;&gt; &gt; serious build tool for build engineers, it is a toy or playground for&#010;&gt; &gt; Scala&#010;&gt; &gt; hackers who thrive on the abstruse. Don't get me wrong, I love Scala, but&#010;&gt; &gt; creating a build tool around .scala files just invites the use of chicken&#010;&gt; &gt; tracks and obscure overly concise cleverness that leads to one WTF&#010;&gt; &gt; experience after another. *It is actually possible to write Scala code&#010;&gt; &gt; that you can reason about,* but it just as easy to write Scala code that&#010;&gt; &gt; resembles APL, and reasoning about build engineering was clearly not a&#010;&gt; &gt; priority with the designers of SBT.&#010;&gt; &gt; &#010;&gt; &gt; The Scala-IDE was a really great approach because it leveraged off of an&#010;&gt; &gt; existing IDE infrastructure such as Eclipse, rather than trying to write&#010;&gt; &gt; an&#010;&gt; &gt; IDE from scratch the way SBT does. I have used Maven for plenty of Scala and Akka projects, but never for&#010;a Play project as Play seems to have its own idea of application&#010;structure and layout and it is easier to just stick with it for Play.&#010;&#010;On 3 December 2014 at 19:11, Eric Kolotyluk &lt;eric.kolotyluk@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; Does anyone know of a good emotional support group for people trying to use&#010;&gt; Maven with Typesafe projects such as Akka and Play?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I was thinking maybe there could a buddy/sponsor system, such as used in AA&#010;&gt; and other self help groups. Maybe there might be group sessions where people&#010;&gt; can talk about their trauma, especially by being constantly invalidated by&#010;&gt; comments such as "you should use the simple build tool SBT, cause, well you&#010;&gt; know, it's simple and easy to use."&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Seriously though, is there a community of people who are successfully using&#010;&gt; Maven with Akka an Play projects? I would love to meet you.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I can see why people who have tried Maven naturally think "oh, its' too&#010;&gt; complicated, anyone can write a simple build tool that does what Maven&#010;&gt; does." Clearly they do not appreciate what Maven is or what it does. SBT and&#010;&gt; Gradle are two great examples of projects that attempted to do something&#010;&gt; more simple, but in the end, really don't measure up.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I personally think the Scala community would be been better served if more&#010;&gt; investment was made in developing better Scala build tools within the Maven&#010;&gt; framework. More and better plugins for Scala, Akka, Play, etc.  Better use&#010;&gt; of&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/sect-scala-script-inline.html&#010;&gt; http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/ch03s03.html&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I don't know if there is a Scala template for writing Maven plugins (or&#010;&gt; mojos), but there should be.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The more I use SBT, the less I like it. It is not what I consider a serious&#010;&gt; build tool for build engineers, it is a toy or playground for Scala hackers&#010;&gt; who thrive on the abstruse. Don't get me wrong, I love Scala, but creating a&#010;&gt; build tool around .scala files just invites the use of chicken tracks and&#010;&gt; obscure overly concise cleverness that leads to one WTF experience after&#010;&gt; another. /It is actually possible to write Scala code that you can reason&#010;&gt; about,/ but it just as easy to write Scala code that resembles APL, and&#010;&gt; reasoning about build engineering was clearly not a priority with the&#010;&gt; designers of SBT.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The Scala-IDE was a really great approach because it leveraged off of an&#010;&gt; existing IDE infrastructure such as Eclipse, rather than trying to write an&#010;&gt; IDE from scratch the way SBT does. I wish the Scala/Typesafe community had&#010;&gt; taken the same approach with build-tools.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; - Eric&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Adam Retter&#010;&#010;skype: adam.retter&#010;tweet: adamretter&#010;http://www.adamretter.org.uk&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

More and better plugins for Scala, Akka, Play, etc.  Better use&#010;&gt; of&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/sect-&#010;&gt; scala-script-inline.html&#010;&gt; http://books.sonatype.com/mcookbook/reference/ch03s03.html&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I don't know if there is a Scala template for writing Maven plugins (or&#010;&gt; mojos), but there should be.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The more I use SBT, the less I like it. It is not what I consider a&#010;&gt; serious build tool for build engineers, it is a toy or playground for Scala&#010;&gt; hackers who thrive on the abstruse. Don't get me wrong, I love Scala, but&#010;&gt; creating a build tool around .scala files just invites the use of chicken&#010;&gt; tracks and obscure overly concise cleverness that leads to one WTF&#010;&gt; experience after another. /It is actually possible to write Scala code that&#010;&gt; you can reason about,/ but it just as easy to write Scala code that&#010;&gt; resembles APL, and reasoning about build engineering was clearly not a&#010;&gt; priority with the designers of SBT.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The Scala-IDE was a really great approach because it leveraged off of an&#010;&gt; existing IDE infrastructure such as Eclipse, rather than trying to write an&#010;&gt; IDE from scratch the way SBT does. I wish the Scala/Typesafe community had&#010;&gt; taken the same approach with build-tools.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; - Eric&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Some forums are more concerned about form than content.&#010;Everyone here is pretty focused on solving your problem rather than &#010;telling how to post it.&#010;&#010;If you look at the examples in my post, you will see that the type is &#010;"pom" for dependencies on libraries.&#010;We also use "provided" scope since we install the libraries once rather &#010;than include them with each upload of a war file since they generally &#010;don't change.&#010;&#010;We set the content of our libraries (jars and versions) at the beginning &#010;of a release cycle and don't change them for the duration of the release &#010;unless there is an emergency.&#010;This gives everyone a stable environment and once you have the libraries &#010;loaded into Tomcat, in our case, they do not change as the application &#010;gets worked on.&#010;This makes the testing go quicker since you are only replacing the war &#010;file that you are working on and the war file only contains the code &#010;that we write.&#010;&#010;I am not sure if this applies to your libraries.&#010;&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;On 05/12/2014 12:04 PM, Mark Eggers wrote:&#010;&gt; -----BEGIN PGP SIGNED MESSAGE-----&#010;&gt; Hash: SHA1&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Ron,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks for the link. Re: Using shaded JAR as a dependency in a WAR module  
Date  :-
Fri, 05 Dec 2014 20:22:52 GMT

-----BEGIN PGP SIGNED MESSAGE-----&#010;Hash: SHA1&#010;&#010;Ron and Stephen,&#010;&#010;Ron, we cannot use libraries installed into Tomcat's&#010;$CATALINA_BASE/lib directory for several reasons. While it's nice from&#010;a developer and deployment point of view, we do end up running&#010;multiple versions of the WAR file (with different versions of various&#010;dependencies) on the same Tomcat. We also release the WAR file, and it&#010;would be difficult to require people to modify their server environment.&#010;&#010;Thanks! I finally figured it out.&#010;&#010;1. Issue number 1&#010;&#010;I was using a POM artifact to aggregate a set of lower level&#010;libraries. In order to do this, I had to set the following in the&#010;shade plugin:&#010;&#010;&lt;promoteTransitiveDependencies&gt;true&lt;/promoteTransitiveDependencies&gt;&#010;&#010;This of course makes perfect sense.&#010;&#010;2. Issue number 2&#010;&#010;I needed to set the following:&#010;&#010;&lt;keepDependenciesWithProvidedScope&gt;true&lt;/keepDependenciesWithProvidedScope&gt;&#010;&#010;Both of these are mentioned (albeit not as clearly as it might be) in&#010;the fine documentation here:&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-shade-plugin/shade-mojo.html&#010;&#010;Combining those two creates a JAR with all of the dependency pom.xml&#010;files in it, as well as the classes / resources / etc. An examination&#010;of the target WAR file shows a nice, clean WEB-INF/lib with managed&#010;dependencies all the way down the chain.&#010;&#010;For those people interested, the dependencies and shade plugin&#010;configuration are given below.&#010;&#010;&lt;dependencies&gt;&#010;    &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;        &lt;groupId&gt;org.mdeggers&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;        &lt;artifactId&gt;Calhost&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;        &lt;version&gt;${calhost.version}&lt;/version&gt;&#010;    &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;    &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;        &lt;groupId&gt;org.mdeggers&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;        &lt;artifactId&gt;IHomeResources&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;        &lt;version&gt;${ihomeresources.version}&lt;/version&gt;&#010;        &lt;type&gt;pom&lt;/type&gt;&#010;    &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&lt;/dependencies&gt;&#010;&#010;&lt;build&gt;&#010;    &lt;plugins&gt;&#010;        &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;            &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;            &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-shade-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;            &lt;version&gt;2.3&lt;/version&gt;&#010;            &lt;executions&gt;&#010;                &lt;execution&gt;&#010;                    &lt;id&gt;combine&lt;/id&gt;&#010;                    &lt;phase&gt;package&lt;/phase&gt;&#010;                    &lt;goals&gt;&#010;                        &lt;goal&gt;shade&lt;/goal&gt;&#010;                    &lt;/goals&gt;&#010;                    &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&#010;&lt;keepDependenciesWithProvidedScope&gt;true&lt;/keepDependenciesWithProvidedScope&gt;&#010;&#010;&lt;promoteTransitiveDependencies&gt;true&lt;/promoteTransitiveDependencies&gt;&#010;                        &lt;artifactSet&gt;&#010;                            &lt;includes&gt;&#010;                                &lt;include&gt;org.mdeggers:*&lt;/include&gt;&#010;                            &lt;/includes&gt;&#010; Hope this is the correct solution.&#010;&#010;. . . just my two cents&#010;/mde/&#010;&#010;On 12/5/2014 10:57 AM, Ron Wheeler wrote:&#010;&gt; Some forums are more concerned about form than content. Everyone&#010;&gt; here is pretty focused on solving your problem rather than telling&#010;&gt; how to post it.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; If you look at the examples in my post, you will see that the type&#010;&gt; is "pom" for dependencies on libraries. We also use "provided"&#010;&gt; scope since we install the libraries once rather than include them&#010;&gt; with each upload of a war file since they generally don't change.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; We set the content of our libraries (jars and versions) at the&#010;&gt; beginning of a release cycle and don't change them for the duration&#010;&gt; of the release unless there is an emergency. This gives everyone a&#010;&gt; stable environment and once you have the libraries loaded into&#010;&gt; Tomcat, in our case, they do not change as the application gets&#010;&gt; worked on. This makes the testing go quicker since you are only&#010;&gt; replacing the war file that you are working on and the war file&#010;&gt; only contains the code that we write.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I am not sure if this applies to your libraries.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Ron&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; On 05/12/2014 12:04 PM, Mark Eggers wrote: Ron,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Thanks for the link. Drive the entire project with an agregator&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; pom.xml&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; The JAR module does shade properly, creating a single JAR&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; with all of the dependencies bundled into a single JAR. Great.&#010;I hope that the discussion was helpful even if you found a better solution.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;On 05/12/2014 3:22 PM, Mark Eggers wrote:&#010;&gt; -----BEGIN PGP SIGNED MESSAGE-----&#010;&gt; Hash: SHA1&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Ron and Stephen,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Ron, we cannot use libraries installed into Tomcat's&#010;&gt; $CATALINA_BASE/lib directory for several reasons. While it's nice from&#010;&gt; a developer and deployment point of view, we do end up running&#010;&gt; multiple versions of the WAR file (with different versions of various&#010;&gt; dependencies) on the same Tomcat. We also release the WAR file, and it&#010;&gt; would be difficult to require people to modify their server environment.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks! I finally figured it out.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 1. Issue number 1&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I was using a POM artifact to aggregate a set of lower level&#010;&gt; libraries. In order to do this, I had to set the following in the&#010;&gt; shade plugin:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;promoteTransitiveDependencies&gt;true&lt;/promoteTransitiveDependencies&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; This of course makes perfect sense.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2. Issue number 2&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I needed to set the following:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;keepDependenciesWithProvidedScope&gt;true&lt;/keepDependenciesWithProvidedScope&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Both of these are mentioned (albeit not as clearly as it might be) in&#010;&gt; the fine documentation here:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-shade-plugin/shade-mojo.html&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Combining those two creates a JAR with all of the dependency pom.xml&#010;&gt; files in it, as well as the classes / resources / etc. An examination&#010;&gt; of the target WAR file shows a nice, clean WEB-INF/lib with managed&#010;&gt; dependencies all the way down the chain.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; For those people interested, the dependencies and shade plugin&#010;&gt; configuration are given below.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;dependencies&gt;&#010;&gt;      &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;          &lt;groupId&gt;org.mdeggers&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;          &lt;artifactId&gt;Calhost&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;          &lt;version&gt;${calhost.version}&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;      &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;      &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;          &lt;groupId&gt;org.mdeggers&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;          &lt;artifactId&gt;IHomeResources&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;          &lt;version&gt;${ihomeresources.version}&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;          &lt;type&gt;pom&lt;/type&gt;&#010;&gt;      &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;/dependencies&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;build&gt;&#010;&gt;      &lt;plugins&gt;&#010;&gt;          &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;              &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;              &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-shade-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;              &lt;version&gt;2.3&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;              &lt;executions&gt;&#010;&gt;                  &lt;execution&gt;&#010;&gt;                      &lt;id&gt;combine&lt;/id&gt;&#010;&gt;                      &lt;phase&gt;package&lt;/phase&gt;&#010;&gt;                      &lt;goals&gt;&#010;&gt;                          &lt;goal&gt;shade&lt;/goal&gt;&#010;&gt;                      &lt;/goals&gt;&#010;&gt;                      &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;keepDependenciesWithProvidedScope&gt;true&lt;/keepDependenciesWithProvidedScope&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;promoteTransitiveDependencies&gt;true&lt;/promoteTransitiveDependencies&gt;&#010;&gt;                          &lt;artifactSet&gt;&#010;&gt;                              &lt;includes&gt;&#010;&gt;                                  &lt;include&gt;org.mdeggers:*&lt;/include&gt;&#010;&gt;                              &lt;/includes&gt;&#010;&gt;      &lt;/plugins&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;/build&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Sorry for the line length.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Obviously, if you don't have any transitive dependencies, you won't&#010;&gt; need the promote line.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; It works. Hope this is the correct solution.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; . . . just my two cents&#010;&gt; /mde/&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 12/5/2014 10:57 AM, Ron Wheeler wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt; Some forums are more concerned about form than content. Everyone&#010;&gt;&gt; here is pretty focused on solving your problem rather than telling&#010;&gt;&gt; how to post it.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; If you look at the examples in my post, you will see that the type&#010;&gt;&gt; is "pom" for dependencies on libraries. We also use "provided"&#010;&gt;&gt; scope since we install the libraries once rather than include them&#010;&gt;&gt; with each upload of a war file since they generally don't change.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; We set the content of our libraries (jars and versions) at the&#010;&gt;&gt; beginning of a release cycle and don't change them for the duration&#010;&gt;&gt; of the release unless there is an emergency. This gives everyone a&#010;&gt;&gt; stable environment and once you have the libraries loaded into&#010;&gt;&gt; Tomcat, in our case, they do not change as the application gets&#010;&gt;&gt; worked on. This makes the testing go quicker since you are only&#010;&gt;&gt; replacing the war file that you are working on and the war file&#010;&gt;&gt; only contains the code that we write.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I am not sure if this applies to your libraries.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Ron&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; On 05/12/2014 12:04 PM, Mark Eggers wrote: Ron,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Thanks for the link. without using the shade plugin.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The entire list of dependencies for the WAR module:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;dependencies&gt; &lt;dependency&gt; &lt;groupId&gt;org.mdeggers&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The&#010;&gt;&gt; last dependency is the shaded JAR, and the one that is not behaving&#010;&gt;&gt; as expected (but probably as built / configured).&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The NetBeans graphical display of the dependencies shows&#010;&gt;&gt; IFCResources, as well as the three components it was shaded from.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Sorry for the top-post. Drive the entire project with an agregator&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; pom.xml&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; The JAR module does shade properly, creating a single JAR&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; with all of the dependencies bundled into a single JAR. Instead, I get all of the dependencies as&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; individual JAR files in WEB-INF/lib.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; I'm using the following environment (can post my complete&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; -----BEGIN PGP SIGNED MESSAGE-----&#010;Hash: SHA1&#010;&#010;Ron,&#010;&#010;I'm not sure if it's a better or worse solution. It does minimize the&#010;configuration effort. This is always a good thing when moving people&#010;from Ant to Maven.&#010;&#010;What it does illustrate (at least to me) is that the code base I'm&#010;working with has more technical debts that need to be addressed.&#010;&#010;Also, that the documentation is quite dense - you speed through it at&#010;your peril.&#010;&#010;. . . just my two cents&#010;/mde/&#010;&#010;On 12/5/2014 7:36 PM, Ron Wheeler wrote:&#010;&gt; Great. I hope that the discussion was helpful even if you found a&#010;&gt; better solution.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Ron&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; On 05/12/2014 3:22 PM, Mark Eggers wrote: Ron and Stephen,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Ron, we cannot use libraries installed into Tomcat's &#010;&gt; $CATALINA_BASE/lib directory for several reasons. While it's nice&#010;&gt; from a developer and deployment point of view, we do end up&#010;&gt; running multiple versions of the WAR file (with different versions&#010;&gt; of various dependencies) on the same Tomcat. We also release the&#010;&gt; WAR file, and it would be difficult to require people to modify&#010;&gt; their server environment.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Thanks! I finally figured it out.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; 1. Issue number 1&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I was using a POM artifact to aggregate a set of lower level &#010;&gt; libraries. In order to do this, I had to set the following in the &#010;&gt; shade plugin:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;promoteTransitiveDependencies&gt;true&lt;/promoteTransitiveDependencies&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;  This of course makes perfect sense.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; 2. Issue number 2&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I needed to set the following:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;keepDependenciesWithProvidedScope&gt;true&lt;/keepDependenciesWithProvidedScope&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Both of these are mentioned (albeit not as clearly as it might be)&#010;&gt; in the fine documentation here:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-shade-plugin/shade-mojo.html&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Combining those two creates a JAR with all of the dependency&#010;&gt; pom.xml files in it, as well as the classes / resources / etc. An&#010;&gt; examination of the target WAR file shows a nice, clean WEB-INF/lib&#010;&gt; with managed dependencies all the way down the chain.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; For those people interested, the dependencies and shade plugin &#010;&gt; configuration are given below.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;dependencies&gt; &lt;dependency&gt; &lt;groupId&gt;org.mdeggers&lt;/groupId&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;artifactId&gt;Calhost&lt;/artifactId&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;version&gt;${calhost.version}&lt;/version&gt; &lt;/dependency&gt; &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;&#010;&gt; &lt;groupId&gt;org.mdeggers&lt;/groupId&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;artifactId&gt;IHomeResources&lt;/artifactId&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;version&gt;${ihomeresources.version}&lt;/version&gt; &lt;type&gt;pom&lt;/type&gt;&#010;&#010;&gt; &lt;/dependency&gt; &lt;/dependencies&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;build&gt; &lt;plugins&gt; &lt;plugin&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-shade-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt; &lt;version&gt;2.3&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&#010;&gt; &lt;executions&gt; &lt;execution&gt; &lt;id&gt;combine&lt;/id&gt; &lt;phase&gt;package&lt;/phase&gt;&#010;&#010;&gt; &lt;goals&gt; &lt;goal&gt;shade&lt;/goal&gt; &lt;/goals&gt; &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;keepDependenciesWithProvidedScope&gt;true&lt;/keepDependenciesWithProvidedScope&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;promoteTransitiveDependencies&gt;true&lt;/promoteTransitiveDependencies&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &#010;&lt;artifactSet&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;includes&gt; &lt;include&gt;org.mdeggers:*&lt;/include&gt; &#010;&gt; Obviously, if you don't have any transitive dependencies, you&#010;&gt; won't need the promote line.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; It works. Hope this is the correct solution.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; . . . just my two cents /mde/&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; On 12/5/2014 10:57 AM, Ron Wheeler wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Some forums are more concerned about form than content.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Everyone here is pretty focused on solving your problem&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; rather than telling how to post it.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; If you look at the examples in my post, you will see that the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; type is "pom" for dependencies on libraries. We also use&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; "provided" scope since we install the libraries once rather&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; than include them with each upload of a war file since they&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; generally don't change.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; We set the content of our libraries (jars and versions) at&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; the beginning of a release cycle and don't change them for&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; the duration of the release unless there is an emergency.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; This gives everyone a stable environment and once you have&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; the libraries loaded into Tomcat, in our case, they do not&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; change as the application gets worked on. This makes the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; testing go quicker since you are only replacing the war file&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; that you are working on and the war file only contains the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; code that we write.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; I am not sure if this applies to your libraries.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Ron&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; On 05/12/2014 12:04 PM, Mark Eggers wrote: Ron,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Thanks for the link. Break up the WAR project into a WAR module and a&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; JAR module 2. Make the WAR module be dependent on the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; JAR module 3. Use the Maven shade plugin in the JAR&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; module to create a shaded JAR 4. Drive the entire&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; project with an agregator pom.xml&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; The JAR module does shade properly, creating a single&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; JAR with all of the dependencies bundled into a single&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; JAR. It uses a pom dependency to gather in most of its&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; requirements. None of the JAR or pom dependencies have&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; further dependencies, so the resulting JAR is&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; self-contained.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; However, when I build the WAR file and reference the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; shaded JAR file as a dependency, I do not get the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; shaded JAR file in WEB-INF/lib. Instead, I get all of&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; the dependencies as individual JAR files in&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; WEB-INF/lib.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; On Friday, December 5, 2014, Yaron Goldstein &lt;yarongoldstein10@gmail.com&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; You can copy it to any directory of choice.&#010;&gt; One thing to remember is to run it in the validate phase:&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;Doing so well up to this point&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; mvn validate install ....&#010;&#010;&#010;And then shows lack of understanding of maven's lifecycle.&#010;&#010;`validate` is the second phase in the standard lifecycle and `install` is&#010;the second last phase in the standard lifecycle.&#010;&#010;Typing `mvn validate install` will ask maven to run all the phases of the&#010;standard lifecycle up to and including the `validate` phase *and then* run&#010;all the phases of the standard lifecycle up to and including the `install`&#010;phase.&#010;&#010;If you are paying attention you will notice that the above command would&#010;execute the plugins bound to the `validate` phase twice&#010;&#010;There is also some subtlety around how that will behave in a multi-module&#010;reactor... The first validate will be applied to *all* modules *and then*&#010;the second validate will be applied to all modules again... Essentially&#010;processing the reactor twice&#010;&#010;Finally, if you really understand maven you probably should be using the&#010;`verify` phase in examples rather than continuing the habit of polluting&#010;the local repo cache with the `install` phase (though some IDEs and&#010;sub-module workflows need it... A build is better if it will work from a&#010;clean repo with just `mvn verify`)&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; More info here&#010;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-antrun-plugin/usage.html&#010;&gt; Good luck &amp; Shalom!!&#010;&gt; Yaron&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Fri, Dec 5, 2014 at 6:06 PM, Aitor Iturriondobeitia &lt;&#010;&gt; laudio.info@gmail.com &lt;javascript:;&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Thanks&#010;&gt; &gt; I must copy the file to one dir out of the project. Hi,&#010;&#010;I have a new challenge for your maven-indexer expertise :)&#010;&#010;What about adding additional information to the local index? I see the&#010;default indexers (min, etc..) produce really minimal information. The&#010;problem is that everybody is using these default indexers and all the&#010;available indexes (maven central, etc) offer very little information that&#010;you can actually use to make the index useful in an application outside of&#010;really basic name, description, group, artifact, etc queries.&#010;&#010;For instance, if I would want to add author information (to query by&#010;author) or dependency information (to perform compatibility checks against&#010;an installation/group of installed artifacts) or anything else for the&#010;matter, what would be the recommended approach?&#010;&#010;&gt;From what I have currently researched, I see 2 options:&#010;&#010;1) Have a custom IndexCreator that uses the updateDocument(ArtifactInfo&#010;artifactInfo, Document document) method to fetch (HTTP GET) get the pom.xml&#010;by using information from the artifactInfo object (repository, groupID,&#010;artifactId, classifier, version, etc.) so that the resulting document&#010;contains the extra information. It seems that IndexCreators are used a lot&#010;more than they are advertised in the descriptions, not only for indexing&#010;new items, but also when converting between ArtifactInfo objects and Lucene&#010;Documents.&#010;&#010;1.1) I had initially started going on this pat, but then I realized that&#010;the artifactInfo that I receive in this method does not provide basic&#010;information (i.e. artifactInfo.getRepository() always returns null ;-( ) It&#010;would be awesome if information like context and/or repository would be&#010;added to the artifactInfo object (maybe in&#010;IndexUtils.constructArtifactInfo( Document doc, IndexingContext context )&#010;?), the same way the ArtifactInfo.UINFO and ArtifactInfo.LAST_MODIFIED&#010;fields are handled specially and explicitly added to a new Document that is&#010;passed to the IndexCreators.&#010;&#010;2) Handle this separately from maven indexer's work, and do it right after&#010;index/update operations, i.e. let maven-indexer update the local index with&#010;information from the remote index and then start manipulating the&#010;underlying Lucene index by adding information retrieved from the network&#010;(HTTP GET) from the remote repositoy's POM files. In a rough pseudocode,&#010;something like:&#010;&#010;indexer.update(repoX);&#010;indexer.getAllIndexedArtifacts().forEach(artifact -&gt;&#010;  var extraData = getExtraData(repoX, artifact);&#010;  var indexer.getLuceneIndex().add(artifact, extraData)&#010;);&#010;&#010;3) Any other suggestions?&#010;&#010;My ultimate goal is (besides basic name/description queries) to be able to&#010;perform compatibility queries on artifacts coming from multiple&#010;repositories, so I need to find a solution to add this missing infrmation&#010;(artifact dependencies, and maybe more).&#010;&#010;As previously, your help and suggestions are most welcomed.&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;Eduard&#010;&#010;On Wed, Nov 26, 2014 at 1:22 PM, Eduard Moraru &lt;enygma2002@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Tue, Nov 25, 2014 at 12:22 PM, Tamas Cservenak &lt;tamas@cservenak.net&gt;&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Hi there,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 1) yes, indexing context retains the artefact “origin” (ie. repo), so you&#010;&gt;&gt; need context per origin. Sadly, the 1 index per context is current&#010;&gt;&gt; limitation of maven indexer, but this problem is known. Created&#010;&gt;&gt; http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MINDEXER-93&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 2) Yes, merged context is basically delegating to member contexts. under&#010;&gt;&gt; the hud, it uses Lucene’s MultiReader to actually perform the search.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have solved the search problem for now by using the SearchEngine&#010;&gt; component and issuing an IteratorSearchRequest on a list of&#010;&gt; IndexingContexts to get paginated results. Will have to see how that works&#010;&gt; on the long run.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt; Eduard&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Re ranging, there are already issues (or problem spread across multiple&#010;&gt;&gt; issues), most notably this one&#010;&gt;&gt; http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MINDEXER-8&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 3) I think yes. Currently, indexer is being transitioned from Plexus to&#010;&gt;&gt; JSR330, and as you see in examples, it should work with any container&#010;&gt;&gt; supporting it. re “manually wiring”, in latest releases you might be able&#010;&gt;&gt; to do it, but in older ones probably not, as Plexus supported field&#010;&gt;&gt; injection only, and some of those member was not exposed via getter/setter.&#010;&gt;&gt; See&#010;&gt;&gt; http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MINDEXER-80&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; --&#010;&gt;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt;&gt; ~t~&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; On 21 Nov 2014 at 18:08:26, Eduard Moraru (enygma2002@gmail.com) wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I have recently started playing with the maven indexer [1], following the&#010;&gt;&gt; examples [2], and I have some questions (since AFAIS, documentation is&#010;&gt;&gt; practically unexistent on the matter):&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 1) From what I can understand, you need an IndexingContext for each&#010;&gt;&gt; repository you plan to index.
