Hi Eduard,&#010;&#010;for additional information see:&#010;http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MINDEXER-81&#010;&#010;Currently, the ArtifactInfo is hardwired, is not extensible.&#010;&#010;Re available index for Central, it’s not the “minimal usable” &#010;the decision driver, but the SIZE of the index download instead.&#010;We were experimenting with different creators, but the bandwidth&#010;it took off (if you compared it to artifact downloads) was really huge.&#010;&#010;As almost everyone uses MRMs, and they tend to “improve” the&#010;basic GAV index Central publishes (ie. once Nexus caches a &#010;JAR file, it will “improve” the index with Classnames in the JAR too,&#010;something Central does not publish).&#010;&#010;artifactInfo#repoId should not return null, if asked via context.&#010;If it does, there is a bug lurking somewhere.&#010;&#010;Currently the “extra info” path is viable, but that would create a lot&#010;of cruft around indexer classes…..&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Thanks,&#010;~t~&#010;&#010;On 8 Dec 2014 at 17:15:08, Eduard Moraru (enygma2002@gmail.com) wrote:&#010;&#010;Hi,  &#010;&#010;I have a new challenge for your maven-indexer expertise :)  &#010;&#010;What about adding additional information to the local index? I see the  &#010;default indexers (min, etc..) produce really minimal information. The  &#010;problem is that everybody is using these default indexers and all the  &#010;available indexes (maven central, etc) offer very little information that  &#010;you can actually use to make the index useful in an application outside of  &#010;really basic name, description, group, artifact, etc queries.  &#010;&#010;For instance, if I would want to add author information (to query by  &#010;author) or dependency information (to perform compatibility checks against  &#010;an installation/group of installed artifacts) or anything else for the  &#010;matter, what would be the recommended approach?  &#010;&#010;From what I have currently researched, I see 2 options:  &#010;&#010;1) Have a custom IndexCreator that uses the updateDocument(ArtifactInfo  &#010;artifactInfo, Document document) method to fetch (HTTP GET) get the pom.xml  &#010;by using information from the artifactInfo object (repository, groupID,  &#010;artifactId, classifier, version, etc.) so that the resulting document  &#010;contains the extra information. It seems that IndexCreators are used a lot  &#010;more than they are advertised in the descriptions, not only for indexing  &#010;new items, but also when converting between ArtifactInfo objects and Lucene  &#010;Documents.  &#010;&#010;1.1) I had initially started going on this pat, but then I realized that  &#010;the artifactInfo that I receive in this method does not provide basic  &#010;information (i.e. artifactInfo.getRepository() always returns null ;-( ) It  &#010;would be awesome if information like context and/or repository would be  &#010;added to the artifactInfo object (maybe in  &#010;IndexUtils.constructArtifactInfo( Document doc, IndexingContext context )  &#010;?), the same way the ArtifactInfo.UINFO and ArtifactInfo.LAST_MODIFIED  &#010;fields are handled specially and explicitly added to a new Document that is  &#010;passed to the IndexCreators.  &#010;&#010;2) Handle this separately from maven indexer's work, and do it right after  &#010;index/update operations, i.e. let maven-indexer update the local index with  &#010;information from the remote index and then start manipulating the  &#010;underlying Lucene index by adding information retrieved from the network  &#010;(HTTP GET) from the remote repositoy's POM files. In a rough pseudocode,  &#010;something like:  &#010;&#010;indexer.update(repoX);  &#010;indexer.getAllIndexedArtifacts().forEach(artifact -&gt;  &#010;var extraData = getExtraData(repoX, artifact);  &#010;var indexer.getLuceneIndex().add(artifact, extraData)  &#010;);  &#010;&#010;3) Any other suggestions?  &#010;&#010;My ultimate goal is (besides basic name/description queries) to be able to  &#010;perform compatibility queries on artifacts coming from multiple  &#010;repositories, so I need to find a solution to add this missing infrmation  &#010;(artifact dependencies, and maybe more).  &#010;&#010;As previously, your help and suggestions are most welcomed.  &#010;&#010;Thanks,  &#010;Eduard  &#010;&#010;On Wed, Nov 26, 2014 at 1:22 PM, Eduard Moraru &lt;enygma2002@gmail.com&gt; wrote:  &#010;&#010;&gt;  &#010;&gt;  &#010;&gt; On Tue, Nov 25, 2014 at 12:22 PM, Tamas Cservenak &lt;tamas@cservenak.net&gt;  &#010;&gt; wrote:  &#010;&gt;  &#010;&gt;&gt; Hi there,  &#010;&gt;&gt;  &#010;&gt;&gt; 1) yes, indexing context retains the artefact “origin” (ie. repo), so you  &#010;&gt;&gt; need context per origin. I want the build to specify the&#010;version used not the system.&#010;&#010;-Dave&#010;&#010;On Mon, Dec 8, 2014 at 2:41 PM, Hervé BOUTEMY &lt;herve.boutemy@free.fr&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Le lundi 8 décembre 2014 13:01:10 David Hoffer a écrit :&#010;&gt; &gt; I'm contemplating an upgrade of a large Maven 3.0.4 build to 3.2.3, just&#010;&gt; &gt; wondering if anyone knows of either any key gotchas in the upgrade and/or&#010;&gt; &gt; key benefits?&#010;&gt; you should check compatibility issues known with some plugins:&#010;&gt; https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/MAVEN/AetherClassNotFound&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; some are fixed if you're using recent version of the affected plugins,&#010;&gt; some are&#010;&gt; not yet fixed&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; for the benefits, choose your favorite from release notes&#010;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/release-notes-all.html&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; One feature I'm wondering at the outset is...with 3.2.3 can I specify the&#010;&gt; &gt; reporting plugin versions in pluginManagement or does this still need to&#010;&gt; be&#010;&gt; &gt; done manually?&#010;&gt; see https://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MNG-5477&#010;&gt; so changing Maven version is just about avoiding a misleading warning&#010;&gt; What is important is maven-site-plugin version.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; And see https://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MSITE-516&#010;&gt; maven-site-plugin version 3.4 has major improvement regarding&#010;&gt; pluginManagement&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Regards,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Hervé&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; -Dave&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

I don't think the CI Server is an issue as we have lots of flexibility when&#010;we setup those jobs.  The issue is for developer builds.  I'm not clear how&#010;to setup workstations to make it easy to build projects with different&#010;Maven versions.&#010;&#010;Our standard practice is to set M2_HOME to the maven install and then add&#010;%M2_HOME%/bin to the path.&#010;&#010;The suggestion was to not set M2_HOME...okay I thought that was required&#010;but we can not set it.  We still need Maven in our path.  Are you saying&#010;that if I set the path to Maven version X, my build can somehow specify to&#010;use Maven version Y or Z?  All I've seen in Maven thus far is the ability&#010;to specify what version must be used not what version to use, and it's the&#010;later I'm looking for.  I don't want devs to have to reconfigure their&#010;system props to build different code branches.&#010;&#010;-Dave&#010;&#010;On Tue, Dec 9, 2014 at 1:51 AM, Bernd Eckenfels &lt;ecki@zusammenkunft.net&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Am Tue, 09 Dec 2014 09:27:29 +0100&#010;&gt; schrieb Jörg Schaible &lt;joerg.schaible@swisspost.com&gt;:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; One other issue came up in this upgrade. We still need Maven in our path.  Are you saying&#010;&gt; that if I set the path to Maven version X, my build can somehow specify to&#010;&gt; use Maven version Y or Z?  All I've seen in Maven thus far is the ability&#010;&gt; to specify what version must be used not what version to use, and it's the&#010;&gt; later I'm looking for.  I don't want devs to have to reconfigure their&#010;&gt; system props to build different code branches.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; -Dave&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Tue, Dec 9, 2014 at 1:51 AM, Bernd Eckenfels &lt;ecki@zusammenkunft.net&gt;&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Am Tue, 09 Dec 2014 09:27:29 +0100&#010;&gt; &gt; schrieb Jörg Schaible &lt;joerg.schaible@swisspost.com&gt;:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; One other issue came up in this upgrade. Subject  :-
[ANN] License Maven Plugin 1.8 released  
Date  :-
Mon, 08 Dec 2014 20:39:17 GMT  
contents:- 
The Mojo team is pleased to announce the release of the License Maven Plugin, version 1.8.&#010;&#010;&#010;This plugin manages the license of a maven project and its dependencies&#010;(update file headers, download dependencies licenses, check thirdparty&#010;licenses, ...).&#010;&#010;Description&#010;-----------&#010;&#010;This License Plugin has the following goals:&#010;&#010;* license:add-third-party&#010;  Goal to generate the third-party license file. This file contains a list of&#010;  the dependencies and their licenses. Each dependency and it's license is&#010;  displayed on a single line in the format&#010;&#010;   (&lt;license-name&gt;) &lt;project-name&gt; &lt;groupId&gt;:&lt;artifactId&gt;:&lt;version&gt;&#010;-&#010;  &lt;project-url&gt;&#010;  It will also copy it in the class-path (says add the generated directory as a&#010;  resource of the build).&#010;&#010;* license:aggregate-add-third-party&#010;  This aggregator goal (will be executed only once and only on pom projects)&#010;  executed the add-third-party on all his modules (in a parellel build cycle)&#010;  then aggreates all the third-party files in final one in the pom project.&#010;&#010;* license:check-file-header&#010;  The goal to check if the state of header on project source files.&#010;&#010;* license:comment-style-list&#010;  Displays all the available comment style to box file headers.&#010;&#010;* license:download-licenses&#010;  Download the license files of all the current project's dependencies, and&#010;  generate a summary file containing a list of all dependencies and their&#010;  licenses.&#010;&#010;* license:license-list&#010;  Display all available licenses.&#010;&#010;* license:third-party-report&#010;  Generates a report of all third-parties detected in the module.&#010;&#010;* license:update-file-header&#010;  The goal to update (or add) the header on project source files. This goal&#010;  replace the update-header goal which can not deal with Copyright. This goal&#010;  use a specific project file descriptor project.xml to describe all files to&#010;  update for a whole project.&#010;&#010;* license:update-project-license&#010;  Updates (or creates) the main project license file according to the given&#010;  license defines as licenseName. Can also generate a bundled license file (to&#010;  avoid collision names in class-path). This file is by default generated in&#010;  META-INF class-path directory.&#010;&#010;Useful links&#010;------------&#010;&#010;Documentation: http://mojo.codehaus.org/license-maven-plugin&#010;JIRA: http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MLICENSE&#010;svn:  https://svn.codehaus.org/mojo/tags/license-maven-plugin-1.8&#010;&#010;To get this update, simply specify the version in your project's plugin&#010;configuration: &#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.codehaus.mojo&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;license-maven-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;1.8&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;The artifacts have been deployed to the mojo repository and will be&#010;mirrored to central.&#010;&#010;Release Notes&#010;-------------&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;    * [MLICENSE-108] - copyright owner is not working properly&#010;    * [MLICENSE-113] - Eclipse Public License includes Eclipse Distribution License by mistake&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team.&#010;&#010;tony&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Tony Chemit&#010;--------------------&#010;tél: +33 (0) 2 40 50 29 28&#010;http://www.codelutin.com&#010;email: chemit@codelutin.com&#010;twitter: https://twitter.com/tchemit&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
[ANN] Animal Sniffer 1.13 Released  
Date  :-
Mon, 08 Dec 2014 20:39:26 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team is pleased to announce the release of Animal Sniffer version 1.13.&#010;&#010;Animal Sniffer provides tools to assist verifying that classes&#010;compiled with a newer JDK/API are compatible with an older JDK/API.&#010;&#010;The following tools are provided by animal sniffer:&#010;&#010;* A command line tool to dump the class file version number&#010;(http://mojo.codehaus.org/animal-sniffer/animal-sniffer/index.html).&#010;This helps you track down the offending jar file when you see&#010;UnsupportedClassVersionError.&#010;&#010;* A set of ANT tasks&#010;(http://mojo.codehaus.org/animal-sniffer/animal-sniffer-ant-tasks/index.html&#010;)&#010;for verifying that your classes comply with an API signature as well&#010;as tasks for creating API signatures from a JDK, or a collection or&#010;jar and class files, or a collection of other API signature files, or&#010;combination of these elements.&#010;&#010;* A rule for use in the maven-enforcer-plugin&#010;(&#010;http://mojo.codehaus.org/animal-sniffer/animal-sniffer-enforcer-rule/index.html&#010;)&#010;for verifying that your classes comply with an API signature .&#010;&#010;* A maven plugin&#010;(http://mojo.codehaus.org/animal-sniffer-maven-plugin/index.html) for&#010;verifying that your classes comply with an API signature as well as&#010;for creating API signatures from a JDK, or the current module's&#010;classes, or the current module's dependencies, or a collection of&#010;other API signature files, or combination of these elements.&#010;&#010;The artifacts have are available from the Maven Central repository.&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Mojo's Animal Sniffer - Version 1.13&#010;&#010;** New Feature&#010; * [MANIMALSNIFFER-48] - Resolve signature version from dependencies / dependencyManagement&#010;if unspecified&#010;&#010;The Mojo Team.&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Tony Chemit&#010;--------------------&#010;tél: +33 (0) 2 40 50 29 28&#010;http://www.codelutin.com&#010;email: chemit@codelutin.com&#010;twitter: https://twitter.com/tchemit&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

This is a run-off vote to select the top two options for our new mascot's&#010;name.&#010;&#010;The entries with the highest number of votes will be selected for the final&#010;round. If there is only one entry with the highest number of votes then the&#010;entries with the second highest number of votes will also be included in&#010;the final round.&#010;&#010;The vote will be open for 72 hours.&#010;&#010;The entries are as follows:&#010;&#010;A. Abraham&#010;B. Boo&#010;C. Darth Mowl&#010;D. Jacob&#010;E. Kaboom&#010;F. Moses&#010;G. Rap&#010;H. Shotgun&#010;K. The Maven Owl&#010;L. Ty&#010;&#010;It is not clear whether all of the above suggestions were completely&#010;serious, but I have included them anyway for this first round.&#010;&#010;Please respond with at most your top three in order of preference. I may&#010;not use second or third preferences if we get a sufficient number of votes,&#010;but in the case of a small poll the additional preferences will help.&#010;&#010;In the event of repeated votes from an individual, only the last cast vote&#010;as determined by me will count.&#010;&#010;Any other discussion should happen in a separate thread.&#010;&#010;Thanks&#010;&#010;-Stephen&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
Little documentation issues  
Date  :-
Tue, 09 Dec 2014 16:42:14 GMT  
contents:- 
After using maven for 7+years, I decided that I finally knew enough &#010;about it to read the docs.&#010;I started here - &#010;http://maven.apache.org/guides/getting-started/index.html - and this led &#010;to other pages.&#010;&#010;I have found some places where a little cleaning up might help new users.&#010;There is one BIG issue and a few smaller ones.&#010;&#010;1) &#010;http://maven.apache.org/guides/introduction/introduction-to-the-lifecycle.html&#010;1a)&#010;  "Packaging&#010;&#010;The first, and most common way, is to set the packaging for your project &#010;via the equally named POM element &lt;packaging&gt;. Some of the valid &#010;packaging values are jar, war, ear and pom.&#010;"&#010;Could we have the full list here or a link to a page with the full list &#010;of the "normal" ones?&#010;Could we have a mention that plug-ins can provide new packaging. There &#010;is an example after the table of the Plexus. This discussion would be &#010;better if held together rather than split up with a discussion of &#010;binding and a table between the two parts of the story.&#010;&#010;&#010;1b) In the table following this line "Each packaging contains a list of &#010;goals to bind to a particular phase. For example, thejarpackaging will &#010;bind the following goals to build phases of the default lifecycle." a &#010;heading row would be nice.&#010;&#010;1c)&#010;Plugins are mentioned well before they are defined on the page. It would &#010;be helpful to briefly describe what a plugin is before using it as a &#010;known concept in "A Build Phase is Made Up of Plugin Goals" which never &#010;defines it before dropping "And this is done by declaring the plugin &#010;goals bound to those build phases."&#010;1d)&#010;The definition of plug-in is obscure to say the least "Plugins are &#010;artifacts that provide goals to Maven." Surely there must be a clearer &#010;way to describe the concept of plugin.&#010;This is one of the most important Maven concepts and this is a WTF &#010;definition.&#010;&#010;2) http://maven.apache.org/guides/getting-started/index.html&#010;&#010;2a)How can Maven benefit my development process? -&gt; How can Maven be of &#010;benefit to my development process? -&gt; How can Maven improve my &#010;development process?&#010;More common  English usage although the current wording is not wrong&#010;2b) How do I use plug-ins? -&gt; How do I use plugins?  no hyphen in &#010;plug-in. Whoops plugin!&#010;&#010;2c) How do I use plugins? has no description of what a plugin is.&#010;&#010;3) http://maven.apache.org/guides/mini/guide-configuring-plugins.html&#010;&#010;3a) No definition of what a plugin is; it just starts of with the &#010;assertion that there are 2 types. I am not sure that that statement is &#010;really true or if it is, it is not a very useful categorization.&#010;&#010;3b) It is recommended to always defined each version of the plugins used &#010;by the build to guarantee the build reproducibility. -&gt; It is &#010;recommended  the version of the each plugins used by the build is &#010;specified to guarantee the reproducibility of the build.&#010;A good practice is to specify them in &#010;the&lt;build&gt;&lt;pluginManagement/&gt;&lt;/build&gt;elements for*each*build plugins &#010;(generally, you will define a &lt;pluginManagement/&gt; element in a parent &#010;POM).  -&gt;&#010;  It is a good practice to specify the version in &#010;the&lt;build&gt;&lt;pluginManagement/&gt;&lt;/build&gt;element for*each*plugin. The &#010;&lt;pluginManagement/&gt; element is generally specified in a parent POM so &#010;that the same plugin version is use in all related projects.&#010;&#010;c) "Maven plugins (build and reporting) are configured by specifying &#010;a&lt;configuration&gt;element where the child elements of &#010;the&lt;configuration&gt;element are mapped to fields, or setters, inside your &#010;Mojo (remember that a plug-in consists of one or more Mojos where a Mojo &#010;maps to a goal). "&#010;Remember!!!. This is the first time a Mojo has been mentioned. It has no &#010;definition and if I look it up I get:&#010;&#010;"mo·jo1&#010;'mojo/&#010;nounUS&#010;a magic charm, talisman, or spell.&#010;"someone must have their mojo working over at the record company"&#010;magic power.&#010;synonyms:    magic, voodoo, hoodoo, wizardry, sorcery;&#010;"&#010;&#010;No wonder my builds aren't working!&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;Can these be fixed soon.&#010;&#010;Some of them are just little bugs but the lack of a clear definition and &#010;discussion  of plugins at the beginning of the "Getting Started" &#010;documentation is a really big oversight since so much of Maven depends &#010;on the built-in plugins and plugins that are created for special tasks.&#010;&#010;Now that we have a new logo and persona, it is time to fix the docs to &#010;make them more accessible.&#010;&#010;Is there a chance that I may eventually understand Maven!&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ron Wheeler&#010;President&#010;Artifact Software Inc&#010;email: rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;skype: ronaldmwheeler&#010;phone: 866-970-2435, ext 102&#010;&#010;&#010;

Some of the valid packaging&#010;&gt; values are jar, war, ear and pom.&#010;&gt; "&#010;&gt; Could we have the full list here or a link to a page with the full list of&#010;&gt; the "normal" ones?&#010;&gt; Could we have a mention that plug-ins can provide new packaging. There is&#010;&gt; an example after the table of the Plexus. This discussion would be better&#010;&gt; if held together rather than split up with a discussion of binding and a&#010;&gt; table between the two parts of the story.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 1b) In the table following this line "Each packaging contains a list of&#010;&gt; goals to bind to a particular phase. For example, thejarpackaging will bind&#010;&gt; the following goals to build phases of the default lifecycle." a heading&#010;&gt; row would be nice.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 1c)&#010;&gt; Plugins are mentioned well before they are defined on the page. It would&#010;&gt; be helpful to briefly describe what a plugin is before using it as a known&#010;&gt; concept in "A Build Phase is Made Up of Plugin Goals" which never defines&#010;&gt; it before dropping "And this is done by declaring the plugin goals bound to&#010;&gt; those build phases."&#010;&gt; 1d)&#010;&gt; The definition of plug-in is obscure to say the least "Plugins are&#010;&gt; artifacts that provide goals to Maven." Surely there must be a clearer way&#010;&gt; to describe the concept of plugin.&#010;&gt; This is one of the most important Maven concepts and this is a WTF&#010;&gt; definition.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2) http://maven.apache.org/guides/getting-started/index.html&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2a)How can Maven benefit my development process? -&gt; How can Maven be of&#010;&gt; benefit to my development process? -&gt; How can Maven improve my development&#010;&gt; process?&#010;&gt; More common  English usage although the current wording is not wrong&#010;&gt; 2b) How do I use plug-ins? -&gt; How do I use plugins?  no hyphen in plug-in.&#010;&gt; Whoops plugin!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2c) How do I use plugins? has no description of what a plugin is.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 3) http://maven.apache.org/guides/mini/guide-configuring-plugins.html&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 3a) No definition of what a plugin is; it just starts of with the&#010;&gt; assertion that there are 2 types. I am not sure that that statement is&#010;&gt; really true or if it is, it is not a very useful categorization.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 3b) It is recommended to always defined each version of the plugins used&#010;&gt; by the build to guarantee the build reproducibility. -&gt; It is recommended&#010;&gt; the version of the each plugins used by the build is specified to guarantee&#010;&gt; the reproducibility of the build.&#010;&gt; A good practice is to specify them in the&lt;build&gt;&lt;pluginManagement/&gt;&lt;/build&gt;elements&#010;&gt; for*each*build plugins (generally, you will define a &lt;pluginManagement/&gt;&#010;&gt; element in a parent POM).  -&gt;&#010;&gt;  It is a good practice to specify the version in&#010;&gt; the&lt;build&gt;&lt;pluginManagement/&gt;&lt;/build&gt;element for*each*plugin. The&#010;&gt; &lt;pluginManagement/&gt; element is generally specified in a parent POM so that&#010;&gt; the same plugin version is use in all related projects.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; c) "Maven plugins (build and reporting) are configured by specifying&#010;&gt; a&lt;configuration&gt;element where the child elements of&#010;&gt; the&lt;configuration&gt;element are mapped to fields, or setters, inside your&#010;&gt; Mojo (remember that a plug-in consists of one or more Mojos where a Mojo&#010;&gt; maps to a goal). I have made some of the changes in the attached file.&#010;&#010;There is not much that can be done until the plugin definition is added.&#010;This definition will clarify a few things and may make it easier to fix &#010;some of the other things.&#010;&#010;There are sentences like this one:&#010;" The second way to add goals to phases is to configure plugins in your &#010;project. Plugins are artifacts that provide&#010;   goals to Maven."&#010;that is written from an odd point of view.&#010;&#010;If I am a Java developer, why would adding more goals be something that &#010;I want to do?&#010;&#010;Each entire sections should be written from a developers point of view. &#010;Rather than adding goals, I may want to perform some special processing &#010;during the build.&#010;This may require the configuration of additional plugins which in turn &#010;might get activated by invoking additional goals (or not).&#010;As a Java developer, I can not add goals unless the goals are part of &#010;the plugin and I would only add goals&#010;a) if the goals were not already in the standard maven build flow AND&#010;b) the goal is available in the plugin.&#010;&#010;I suspect that this is a common problem with the Introductory &#010;documentation that makes it hard for a Java developer to read.&#010;&#010;Can someone suggest a description of "plugin" and "Mojo" that is written &#010;from a developer's point of view but sufficiently close to the technical &#010;reality that it will not cause trouble when someone starts to read the &#010;Plugin Developer's sections.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On 09/12/2014 11:42 AM, Ron Wheeler wrote:&#010;&gt; After using maven for 7+years, I decided that I finally knew enough &#010;&gt; about it to read the docs.&#010;&gt; I started here - &#010;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/guides/getting-started/index.html - and this &#010;&gt; led to other pages.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have found some places where a little cleaning up might help new users.&#010;&gt; There is one BIG issue and a few smaller ones.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 1) &#010;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/guides/introduction/introduction-to-the-lifecycle.html&#010;&gt; 1a)&#010;&gt;  "Packaging&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The first, and most common way, is to set the packaging for your &#010;&gt; project via the equally named POM element &lt;packaging&gt;. Some of the &#010;&gt; valid packaging values are jar, war, ear and pom.&#010;&gt; "&#010;&gt; Could we have the full list here or a link to a page with the full &#010;&gt; list of the "normal" ones?&#010;&gt; Could we have a mention that plug-ins can provide new packaging. It &#010;&gt; would be helpful to briefly describe what a plugin is before using it &#010;&gt; as a known concept in "A Build Phase is Made Up of Plugin Goals" which &#010;&gt; never defines it before dropping "And this is done by declaring the &#010;&gt; plugin goals bound to those build phases."&#010;&gt; 1d)&#010;&gt; The definition of plug-in is obscure to say the least "Plugins are &#010;&gt; artifacts that provide goals to Maven." Surely there must be a clearer &#010;&gt; way to describe the concept of plugin.&#010;&gt; This is one of the most important Maven concepts and this is a WTF &#010;&gt; definition.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2) http://maven.apache.org/guides/getting-started/index.html&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2a)How can Maven benefit my development process? -&gt; How can Maven be &#010;&gt; of benefit to my development process? -&gt; How can Maven improve my &#010;&gt; development process?&#010;&gt; More common  English usage although the current wording is not wrong&#010;&gt; 2b) How do I use plug-ins? -&gt; How do I use plugins?  no hyphen in &#010;&gt; plug-in. Whoops plugin!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2c) How do I use plugins? has no description of what a plugin is.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 3) http://maven.apache.org/guides/mini/guide-configuring-plugins.html&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 3a) No definition of what a plugin is; it just starts of with the &#010;&gt; assertion that there are 2 types. I am not sure that that statement is &#010;&gt; really true or if it is, it is not a very useful categorization.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 3b) It is recommended to always defined each version of the plugins &#010;&gt; used by the build to guarantee the build reproducibility. -&gt; It is &#010;&gt; recommended  the version of the each plugins used by the build is &#010;&gt; specified to guarantee the reproducibility of the build.&#010;&gt; A good practice is to specify them in &#010;&gt; the&lt;build&gt;&lt;pluginManagement/&gt;&lt;/build&gt;elements for*each*build plugins&#010;&#010;&gt; (generally, you will define a &lt;pluginManagement/&gt; element in a parent &#010;&gt; POM).  -&gt;&#010;&gt;  It is a good practice to specify the version in &#010;&gt; the&lt;build&gt;&lt;pluginManagement/&gt;&lt;/build&gt;element for*each*plugin. The &#010;&gt; &lt;pluginManagement/&gt; element is generally specified in a parent POM so &#010;&gt; that the same plugin version is use in all related projects.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; c) "Maven plugins (build and reporting) are configured by specifying &#010;&gt; a&lt;configuration&gt;element where the child elements of &#010;&gt; the&lt;configuration&gt;element are mapped to fields, or setters, inside &#010;&gt; your Mojo (remember that a plug-in consists of one or more Mojos where &#010;&gt; a Mojo maps to a goal). Hi all,&#010;&#010;&gt; Can someone suggest a description of "plugin" and "Mojo" that is&#010;&gt; written from a developer's point of view but sufficiently close to the&#010;&gt; technical reality that it will not cause trouble when someone starts&#010;&gt; to read the Plugin Developer's sections.&#010;&#010;Here's my first cut at it:&#010;&#010;A *plugin* is an extension of Maven that provides additional behavior&#010;during a build. Nearly every aspect of a Maven build is defined as plugins.&#010;For example, the maven-compiler-plugin provides the logic needed to compile&#010;Java classes from sources, and the maven-jar-plugin knows how to packages&#010;those Java classes into JAR files.&#010;&#010;Plugins that are part of the official Maven project are named according to&#010;the pattern "maven-&lt;foo&gt;-plugin", where &lt;foo&gt; relates to the plugin's&#010;purpose (e.g., "compiler" or "jar" as described above). Unofficial plugins,&#010;such as those produced by the Codehaus project, are typically named&#010;according to the pattern "&lt;foo&gt;-maven-plugin" to avoid any implication that&#010;they are somehow official Maven(TM) products.&#010;&#010;Every plugin consists of a collection of *goals*, each of which defines&#010;specific behavior. Some goals automatically become part of the build when&#010;the plugin is declared in your POM, injecting themselves at the appropriate&#010;phase in the build's default lifecycle&#010;&lt;http://maven.apache.org/guides/introduction/introduction-to-the-lifecycle.html&gt;.&#010;Others need to be explicitly bound to the desired phase(s) as *executions*.&#010;Some sophisticated plugins (such as the nar-maven-plugin&#010;&lt;https://github.com/maven-nar/nar-maven-plugin&gt;) even define new phases of&#010;the lifecycle. Each plugin goal is implemented as a mojo&#010;&lt;http://maven.apache.org/developers/mojo-api-specification.html&gt;: a Java&#010;class providing the code necessary to accomplish that specific goal. For&#010;that reason, people sometimes use the terms "goal" and "mojo"&#010;interchangeably.&#010;&#010;The ecosystem of available plugins makes Maven an exceptionally versatile&#010;and powerful tool for managing nearly every imaginable aspect of your&#010;project's build process.&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;P.S. I disclaim all copyright interest in the above. Please use / steal /&#010;edit / tear apart / throw away as you wish.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On Tue, Dec 9, 2014 at 1:58 PM, Ron Wheeler &lt;rwheeler@artifact-software.com&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I have made some of the changes in the attached file.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; There is not much that can be done until the plugin definition is added.&#010;&gt; This definition will clarify a few things and may make it easier to fix&#010;&gt; some of the other things.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; There are sentences like this one:&#010;&gt; " The second way to add goals to phases is to configure plugins in your&#010;&gt; project. contents:- 
Thinking about the developer's perspective a bit, I came up with some&#010;suggestions but no actual language.&#010;&#010;The developer is a person who wants to build units of software into&#010;distributable products, so it's useful to talk briefly about&#010;"lifecycle", "phase", "goal", "execution", and "artifact" in terms&#010;familiar to such a person.  *Briefly* -- full details should be&#010;linked.  This is simply to define terms which will then be used to map&#010;the nature of "Maven plugin" to his experience.&#010;&#010;A developer probably has a general notion of what a "plugin" is, so&#010;what he needs is to know what a *Maven* plugin is: an assembly of Java&#010;classes which provides additional concepts and behaviors that the&#010;Maven framework can use in building your projects.  It can define&#010;additional lifecycles and phases, and it provides goals that you may&#010;bind to phases in order to perform additional work during the build.&#010;There should be a link to how one creates a Maven plugin, elsewhere.&#010;&#010;It may be well to mention at *this* point that much of Maven's&#010;"built-in" behavior is actually provided by included plugins.  In this&#010;way, one first learns what a Maven plugin is and then immediately sees&#010;application of the concept through the lens of the knowledge one has&#010;just gained.  Perhaps pick one common plugin as an example.&#010;&#010;Someone noted that "goal" and "Mojo" are often used interchangeably,&#010;but it may be good to mention here that "goal" is a named behavior and&#010;"Mojo" is its implementation.  (If I have that right.)&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Mark H. Wood&#010;Lead Technology Analyst&#010;&#010;University Library&#010;Indiana University - Purdue University Indianapolis&#010;755 W. Michigan Street&#010;Indianapolis, IN 46202&#010;317-274-0749&#010;www.ulib.iupui.edu&#010;&#010;

One of the wonderful features about Maven is that no matter how long one &#010;has been using it or how much one has studied Maven documentation , one &#010;still feels the necessity of ending every assertion about how it works &#010;with "(If I have that right.)" .&#010;&#010;I am so happy to not be alone!&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;On 10/12/2014 10:48 AM, Mark H. Hi,&#010;&#010;Your are probably missing&#010;&#010;        &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;          &lt;source&gt;1.7&lt;/source&gt;&#010;          &lt;target&gt;1.7&lt;/target&gt;&#010;        &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Basically you are using the 1.7 compiler to compile java5 source code&#010;to java 5 byte code (1.5 is the default value for source/target IIRC)&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On Fri, Dec 12, 2014 at 5:11 PM, jeff_gaer &lt;jeff_gaer@yahoo.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I am building with jdk 1.7 but getting an compiler error that suggests mvn&#010;&gt; is&#010;&gt; using the 1.5 jdk ( which is not installed).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;  error: multi-catch statement is not supported in -source 1.5&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; OS name: "linux", version: "2.6.18-274.el5", arch: "i386", family: "unix"&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have even tried specifically specifying the JDK version in the compile&#010;&gt; plugin&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &lt;plugins&gt;&#010;&gt;          &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;             &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;             &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-compiler-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;             &lt;version&gt;3.2&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;          &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;           &lt;verbose&gt;true&lt;/verbose&gt;&#010;&gt;           &lt;fork&gt;true&lt;/fork&gt;&#010;&gt;           &lt;executable&gt;${JAVA_HOME}/bin/javac&lt;/executable&gt;&#010;&gt;           &lt;compilerVersion&gt;1.7&lt;/compilerVersion&gt;&#010;&gt;         &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;          &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Hello all,&#010;&#010;We also want to build a --project-list with a aggregator pom, so all the&#010;modules of  that pom are getting build. In the mean time, we also want the&#010;dependencies of those module to  build. (So, --also-make). Only we can't&#010;get this to run. Is there anyone who can help with this?&#010;&#010;We were thinking of a Bash or Groovy script to parse the aggregator pom to&#010;build up the --project-list argument.&#010;&#010;Does anyone see an easier way?&#010;&#010;With regards,&#010;&#010;Nick Stolwijk&#010;&#010;~~~ Try to leave this world a little better than you found it and, when&#010;your turn comes to die, you can die happy in feeling that at any rate you&#010;have not wasted your time but have done your best ~~~&#010;&#010;Lord Baden-Powell&#010;&#010;On Tue, May 7, 2013 at 2:39 AM, spoots &lt;spootsy.ootsy@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Thanks for the reply, again :)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I don't think "-amd" covers my need though. Because there's no parent/child&#010;&gt; relationship between the modules/sub-modules there's no dependency between&#010;&gt; them. It feels to me like there's an option missing for the reactor here...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; A simpler example for clarity:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &amp;lt;a&amp;gt;&#010;&gt;   &amp;lt;b&amp;gt;&#010;&gt;     &amp;lt;c /&amp;gt;&#010;&gt;     &amp;lt;d /&amp;gt;&#010;&gt;     &amp;lt;e /&amp;gt;&#010;&gt;   &amp;lt;/b&amp;gt;&#010;&gt;   &amp;lt;f /&amp;gt;&#010;&gt;   &amp;lt;g /&amp;gt;&#010;&gt; &amp;lt;/a&amp;gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Each node is a project, and sub-projects are nested. For dependencies, say&#010;&gt; only that "c depends on f". There are no parent-child relationships.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; If I want to build &amp;lt;b&amp;gt; with all its sub-modules (&amp;lt;c&amp;gt; &amp;lt;d&amp;gt;&#010;&gt; &amp;lt;e&amp;gt;) and dependencies (&amp;lt;f&amp;gt;), can I do that? The only options&#010;I&#010;&gt; see are:&#010;&gt; 1 - change to b directory, then "mvn install"&#010;&gt; 2 - from top level, "mvn install -pl a/b -amd"&#010;&gt; 3 - from top level, "mvn install -pl a/b/c,a/b/d,a/b/e -amd"&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Option 1 builds the sub-modules I want, but doesn't build the dependency&#010;&gt; &amp;lt;f&amp;gt;.&#010;&gt; Option 2 only builds the project &amp;lt;b&amp;gt;, none of it's sub-modules&#010;&gt; because&#010;&gt; they are not dependents.&#010;&gt; Option 3 works, but it's no good because I need to know &amp; provide all the&#010;&gt; sub-modules of &amp;lt;b&amp;gt;.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Ideally there'd be an option like "-ams" (also make sub-modules) which I&#010;&gt; could use in option 2, but I can't see any way to do it?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context:&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Building-selected-projects-with-nested-aggregators-tp5753572p5755076.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
Installing only javadocs  
Date  :-
Mon, 15 Dec 2014 13:13:03 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;I have a continuous integration setup where the build is setup in two &#010;steps. First all modules are built and deployed. After that a second &#010;build is triggered that takes those artifacts and builds installers from &#010;that.&#010;&#010;Because of performance reasons and they are only needed for the &#010;installers, any javadoc jars are only being built in the second step. &#010;Now I want to install these jars into the local repo as well. A call to &#010;javadoc:jar only creates those jars, not copy them over to the local repo.&#010;&#010;I do not want to run mvn install, as that would run the complete build &#010;again. Now, I looked at the documentation of maven-javadoc-plugin and &#010;the maven-install-plugin but I couldnt find a way to only install the &#010;javadocs. (something like mvn javadoc:jar javadoc:install, if such a &#010;goal would exist).&#010;&#010;Is there a way to achieve that or am I on the wrong track?&#010;&#010;Greetings,&#010;&#010;Christian&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Re: Installing only javadocs

Hi Stephen,&#010;&#010;that is actually the way it is setup. With one minor problem, the &#010;installers need the javadocs from the other modules as well. And we do &#010;not build them during the normal built because of performance reasons &#010;(it takes ~15mins to create them).&#010;&#010;You are right, the installer modules could be even completly decoupled, &#010;what we have are submodules that are activated via a profile.&#010;&#010;But to built the javadocs I have to go into the original modules again &#010;and create the javadocs. This so far is working. But in this setup, the &#010;installer modules have no access to the javadocs, since they onlide &#010;reside inside the target folders and not the local repository.&#010;&#010;Maybe to illustrate:&#010;&#010;Main module:&#010;   root/module/A&#010;              /B&#010;              /C&#010;              /D/D1&#010;                /D2&#010;&#010;Installer:&#010;   root/installers/instA&#010;                  /instB&#010;&#010;&#010;What I currently run is mvn deployin the main build, with disabled &#010;javadoc generation.&#010;For the installers, I runmvn javadoc:jarin the main module directory, &#010;and then mvn installin the installer directory. But again, javadoc:jar &#010;does not copy to local repo, so when the installers are run the &#010;(possibly) reference old javadocs that are still in the local repo, &#010;instead of using the just generated javadocs.&#010;&#010;Hope this clarifies the problem&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;Christian&#010;&#010;On 15.12.2014 15:47, Stephen Connolly wrote:&#010;&gt; Wrong track.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 15 December 2014 at 13:13, Christian Domsch &lt;mail@landrus.de&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I have a continuous integration setup where the build is setup in two&#010;&gt;&gt; steps. Tue, 16 Dec 2014 10:30:19 GMT  
contents:- 
Hello everybody,&#010;&#010;My team is currently migrating a legacy Ant project with a bad Subversion layout to Maven.&#010;We're running into 2 problems with the Maven scm configuration.&#010;Let me first sketch the Subversion layout:&#010;&#010;ROOT&#010;  - trunk&#010;  -- department&#010;      - parent&#010;        - pom.xml&#010;      - project1&#010;        - pom.xml (inherits parent)&#010;      - project2&#010;        - pom.xml (inherits parent)&#010;      - release&#010;        - pom.xml (inherits parent)&#010;  - branches&#010;    - feature1&#010;      - department&#010;        - parent&#010;          - pom.xml&#010;        - project1&#010;          - pom.xml (inherits parent)&#010;        - project2&#010;          - pom.xml (inherits parent)&#010;        - release&#010;          - pom.xml (inherits parent)&#010;  - tags&#010;    - ...&#010;&#010;When developping code, we work on branches, we then merge back to trunk and at some point&#010;we make a new branch from trunk for the release.&#010;Since we have our trunk and branches on a higher level than the projects, we would have to&#010;add the branch name in the &lt;scm&gt; URL to gain a full path.&#010;Of course this is not what we want, because the Maven release plugin won't know how to make&#010;tags etc.&#010;One possibility might be to use a compound of 2 variables (base url and branch name) and a&#010;relative path, but this feels like a very dirty workaround.&#010;Does any of you have experience with a setup like this?&#010;&#010;Kind regards,&#010;&#010;Melvyn de Kort&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Adrien Rivard &lt;adrien.riv...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Maven follows symlinks  
Date  :-
Wed, 17 Dec 2014 13:06:09 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;I'm not sure what you are trying to do, but mvn eclipse:eclipse is a&#010;totally deprecated way to use maven in eclipse.&#010;&#010;Now the way is to let m2e handle automatically the .classpath and others&#010;eclipse files on import projects&#010;&#010;That may (or not?) resolve your problem since the jars will now be linked&#010;to the local m2 repo  (~/m2/repo/..)&#010;&#010;&#010;Note that files generated by "mvn eclipse:eclipse" are incompatible with&#010;those generated by m2e so be sure to delete them completely before trying.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Dec 17, 2014 at 1:37 PM, Borzh &lt;borzh62@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have problem with mvn eclipse:eclipse, it generates hard paths in its&#010;&gt; projects, instead of using&#010;&gt; path as it is (symlink).&#010;&gt; How to tell maven not to follow symlinks?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks in advance.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Adrien Rivard&#010;&#010;

Re: Error while creating hadoop package 2.6.0 with Maven 3.2.3  
Date  :-
Fri, 19 Dec 2014 08:52:19 GMT  
contents:- 
So this is not a Maven3 issue, but a JDK8 (kind of) issue. (seems like you  &#010;upgraded the JDK as well)&#010;Oracle introduced with JDK8 a more strict parsing of the javadocs.&#010;&#010;Since the javadoc is incorrect, it fails.&#010;You have 3 options:&#010;- Use JDK7 or less&#010;- Fix the javadoc. The problem here is that &lt;String&gt; and &lt;File&gt; are  &#010;invalid HTML-tags. You should escape it to &amp;lt;String&amp;gt; and &amp;lt;File&amp;gt;&#010;- Add -Xdoclint:none or -Xdoclint:syntax (I think), see docs[1]. This way  &#010;you can suppress these errors.&#010;&#010;The maven-javadoc-plugin still struggles a bit with -Xdoclint[2]. A single  &#010;-Xdoclint argument works fine, multiple is not yet supported(comma  &#010;separation handling fails).&#010;&#010;thanks,&#010;Robert&#010;&#010;[1]  &#010;https://docs.oracle.com/javase/8/docs/technotes/tools/unix/javadoc.html#BEJEFABE&#010;[2] https://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MJAVADOC-387&#010;&#010;Op Fri, 19 Dec 2014 04:03:00 +0100 schreef Martin Gainty  &#010;&lt;mgainty@hotmail.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; take a look at :&#010;&gt; /**&#010;&gt;      * Method getExcludePackageNames.&#010;&gt;      *&#010;&gt;      * @return List&#010;&gt;      */&#010;&gt;     public java.util.List&lt;String&gt; getExcludePackageNames()&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; //if i change&#010;&gt; //@return List to&#010;&gt; //@return List&lt;String&gt;&#010;&gt; //i get the same error you get&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; please file enhancement request at&#010;&gt; https://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MJAVADOC&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; thanks,&#010;&gt; M-&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Date: Fri, 19 Dec 2014 07:50:15 +0530&#010;&gt; Subject: Fwd: Fwd: Error while creating hadoop package 2.6.0 with Maven  &#010;&gt; 3.2.3&#010;&gt; From: venkat.architect@gmail.com&#010;&gt; To: users@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks Robert.&#010;&gt; I did a -e and also a -X, -X option shows error messagesthat are  &#010;&gt; specifically related to 'Unknown tag' for String andFile. Looks like  &#010;&gt; something related to 'Mojo' declaration, butnot sure. I am not a full  &#010;&gt; time developer.&#010;&gt; Anything related to Maven with PATH variable?&#010;&gt; Logs attached.&#010;&gt; Thanks,Venkat.&#010;&gt; On Thu, Dec 18, 2014 at 11:27 PM, Robert Scholte &lt;rfscholte@apache.org&gt;  &#010;&gt; wrote:Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I guess you should be able to resolve the warnings, but that's a  &#010;&gt; different issue.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; When the build of the Apache Hadoop Maven Plugins 2.6.0 starts, I only  &#010;&gt; see "Downloading...."&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Normally this should be followed by "Downloaded...", which means that  &#010;&gt; the download attempt actually succeeded.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; For some reason something goes wrong here.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; You might want to add -e to get a stacktrace, which could give you an  &#010;&gt; extra hint (or worst case, add -X for debug logging)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; thanks,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Robert&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Op Thu, 18 Dec 2014 18:18:51 +0100 schreef Venkat Ramakrishnan  &#010;&gt; &lt;venkat.architect@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&#010;For some reason I am struggling to &#010;create a war and a jar from a maven war project. I want to create these two artifacts from&#010;my maven war project with following requirements -&#010;&#010;Jar&#010; - This should contain all the class files and dependencies of war &#010;project. However dependencies should be copied under lib folder of this &#010;jar and should not be in unpacked form. This part is giving me problem.&#010;&#010;War&#010; - For war I simply want to have static artifacts and nothing which is &#010;present under WEB-INF folder. I am able to achieve this using maven war &#010;plugin.&#010;&#010;Here is the code present under &lt;build&gt; tag of my pom.xml -&#010;&lt;build&gt;&#010;        &lt;plugins&gt;&#010;            &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;                &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-compiler-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;                &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;                    &lt;source&gt;1.8&lt;/source&gt;&#010;                    &lt;target&gt;1.8&lt;/target&gt;&#010;                &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;            &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;            &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;                &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-assembly-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;                &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;                    &lt;descriptors&gt;&#010;                        &lt;descriptor&gt;assembly.xml&lt;/descriptor&gt;&#010;                    &lt;/descriptors&gt;&#010;                    &lt;appendAssemblyId&gt;false&lt;/appendAssemblyId&gt;&#010;                    &lt;archive&gt;&#010;                        &lt;manifest&gt;&#010;                            &lt;addClasspath&gt;true&lt;/addClasspath&gt;&#010;                            &lt;classpathPrefix&gt;lib/&lt;/classpathPrefix&gt;&#010;                        &lt;/manifest&gt;&#010;                    &lt;/archive&gt;&#010;                &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;                &lt;executions&gt;&#010;                    &lt;execution&gt;&#010;                        &lt;id&gt;jar-with-dependencies-in-lib&lt;/id&gt;&#010;                        &lt;phase&gt;package&lt;/phase&gt;&#010;                        &lt;goals&gt;&#010;                            &lt;goal&gt;single&lt;/goal&gt;&#010;                        &lt;/goals&gt;&#010;                    &lt;/execution&gt;&#010;                &lt;/executions&gt;&#010;            &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;            &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;                &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-war-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;                &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;                    &lt;packagingExcludes&gt;WEB-INF/&lt;/packagingExcludes&gt;&#010;                    &lt;failOnMissingWebXml&gt;false&lt;/failOnMissingWebXml&gt;&#010;                &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;            &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;        &lt;/plugins&gt;&#010;    &lt;/build&gt;&#010;&#010;Here is content of assembly.xml file which is located directly under project root directory&#010;- &#010;&#010;&lt;assembly&#010;    xmlns="http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-assembly-plugin/assembly/1.1.2"&#010;    xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"&#010;    xsi:schemaLocation="http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-assembly-plugin/assembly/1.1.2&#010;http://maven.apache.org/xsd/assembly-1.1.2.xsd"&gt;&#010;    &lt;id&gt;jar-with-dependencies-in-lib&lt;/id&gt;&#010;    &lt;formats&gt;&#010;        &lt;format&gt;jar&lt;/format&gt;&#010;    &lt;/formats&gt;&#010;    &lt;includeBaseDirectory&gt;false&lt;/includeBaseDirectory&gt;&#010;    &lt;fileSets&gt;&#010;        &lt;fileSet&gt;&#010;            &lt;directory&gt;target/${project.artifactId}-${project.version}/WEB-INF/lib&lt;/directory&gt;&#010;            &lt;includes&gt;&#010;                &lt;include&gt;target/${project.artifactId}-${project.version}/WEB-INF/classes&lt;/include&gt;&#010;              &lt;/includes&gt;&#010;        &lt;/fileSet&gt;&#010;    &lt;/fileSets&gt;&#010;&lt;/assembly&gt;&#010;&#010;I&#010; feel that I don't need maven-war-plugin at all and both the artifacts &#010;can be created using maven assembly plugin only. However I am unable to &#010;figure out how to achieve this.&#010;&#010;- Shailendra&#010; &#009;&#009; &#009;   &#009;&#009;   &#009;&#009; &#009;   &#009;&#009;  &#010;

Re-reading your request...&#010;&#010;bq. Jar&#010;&#009;- This should contain all the class files and dependencies of war  &#010;project. However dependencies should be copied under lib folder of this  &#010;jar and should not be in unpacked form.&#010;&#010;I hope you are aware that this conflicts with the jar-specs. The classes  &#010;inside the lib/*.jars won't end up on the classpath, which makes this jar  &#010;useless.&#010;I'd strongly advice you not to solve it as you described.&#010;&#010;thanks,&#010;Robert&#010;&#010;Op Fri, 19 Dec 2014 10:33:19 +0100 schreef shailendra singh  &#010;&lt;shailendra_01@outlook.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thank you for your response.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I am already aware about these two parameters.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I don't thing 'archiveClasses' parameter will be of any help in my case.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I had tried to use 'attachClasses' initially but I could not figure out  &#010;&gt; how to pull war dependencies (and that too in a lib folder) in the jar  &#010;&gt; file which will be generated by setting this parameter to true.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So I have no solution for my problem yet.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks&#010;&gt; Shailendra&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; To: users@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt; Subject: Re: Creating a jar and a war from a war project&#010;&gt;&gt; Date: Fri, 19 Dec 2014 09:54:58 +0100&#010;&gt;&gt; From: rfscholte@apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; have a look at the following parameters of the manve-war plugin:&#010;&gt;&gt; - archiveClasses[1]&#010;&gt;&gt; - attachClasses[2]&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I suggest *not* to use the maven-assembly-plugin in this case. Subject  :-
Re: Creating a jar and a war from a war project  
Date  :-
Fri, 19 Dec 2014 13:09:35 GMT  
contents:- 
Starting with an explanation of what you are trying to accomplish rather &#010;than with what problem you are experiencing, usually makes the problem &#010;easier to solve and makes the advice you get actually helpful.&#010;&#010;What are you trying to do that makes your requirements so non-standard?&#010;&#010;If you are just trying to separate the war from the code, this is pretty &#010;standard and a good idea.&#010;You make 2 projects, one to make the jar and another to make the war.&#010;Both become trivial examples of maven projects and do not require any &#010;crazy plug-in configurations.&#010;The war has a dependency on the jar.&#010;&#010;If you want to install the jar separately from your war(jar not included &#010;the war), make the jar dependency in your war POM as scope "provided".&#010;Maven will not put any jar contents in the war file and will leave it up &#010;to the Servlet container to find the classes.&#010;The jar is nothing special and all of the components will be where they &#010;are supposed to be and you will have no trouble when you try to run your &#010;app.&#010;&#010;http://blog.artifact-software.com/tech/?tag=maven has some articles that &#010;I wrote on making multi-project application work with Maven with this &#010;sort of separation of libraries from war configuration.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;On 19/12/2014 5:18 AM, Robert Scholte wrote:&#010;&gt; Re-reading your request...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; bq. Jar&#010;&gt;     - This should contain all the class files and dependencies of war &#010;&gt; project. However dependencies should be copied under lib folder of &#010;&gt; this jar and should not be in unpacked form.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I hope you are aware that this conflicts with the jar-specs. The &#010;&gt; classes inside the lib/*.jars won't end up on the classpath, which &#010;&gt; makes this jar useless.&#010;&gt; I'd strongly advice you not to solve it as you described.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; thanks,&#010;&gt; Robert&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Op Fri, 19 Dec 2014 10:33:19 +0100 schreef shailendra singh &#010;&gt; &lt;shailendra_01@outlook.com&gt;:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Thank you for your response.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I am already aware about these two parameters.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I don't thing 'archiveClasses' parameter will be of any help in my case.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I had tried to use 'attachClasses' initially but I could not figure &#010;&gt;&gt; out how to pull war dependencies (and that too in a lib folder) in &#010;&gt;&gt; the jar file which will be generated by setting this parameter to true.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; So I have no solution for my problem yet.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Thanks&#010;&gt;&gt; Shailendra&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; To: users@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Subject: Re: Creating a jar and a war from a war project&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Date: Fri, 19 Dec 2014 09:54:58 +0100&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; From: rfscholte@apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; have a look at the following parameters of the manve-war plugin:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; - archiveClasses[1]&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; - attachClasses[2]&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; I suggest *not* to use the maven-assembly-plugin in this case. It'll &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; make&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; things over-complex.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; thanks,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Robert&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; [1]&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-war-plugin/war-mojo.html#archiveClasses&#010;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; [2]&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-war-plugin/war-mojo.html#attachClasses&#010;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Op Fri, 19 Dec 2014 08:03:22 +0100 schreef shailendra singh&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &lt;shailendra_01@outlook.com&gt;:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &gt; For some reason I am struggling to&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &gt; create a war and a jar from a maven war project. [ANN] Apache Maven Assembly Plugin 2.5.3 Released  
Date  :-
Fri, 19 Dec 2014 19:11:03 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the&#010;Apache Maven Assembly Plugin, version 2.5.3.&#010;&#010;The Assembly Plugin for Maven is primarily intended to allow users to aggregate&#010;the project output along with its dependencies, modules, site documentation,&#010;and other files into a single distributable archive.&#010;&#010;This release is a bugfix release.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-assembly-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-assembly-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.5.3&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Assembly Plugin - Version 2.5.3&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-648] - lineEnding in fileSet corrupts jar files&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-665] - OS dependent behaviour while packaging&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-735] - NullPointerException at&#010;org.apache.commons.compress.archivers.zip.FallbackZipEncoding.encode(FallbackZipEncoding.java:80)&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-739] - directory permissions are not 755 but 000 in zip&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-741] - wrong paths in file-modes tests&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-742] - Unclosed ZipFile warnings when ZIP archives are included&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-743] - &lt;includeBaseDirectory&gt; not correct&#010;&#010;** Improvement&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-720] - Fixed Checkstyle reported errors / warnings&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-738] - Upgrade to plexus-archiver from 2.8.4 to&#010;2.9.1 and plexus-io from 2.3.5 to 2.4.1&#010;&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;
